Allah's Existence
beginner

The Creed of Monotheism in the Religion of Ibrahim
Quranic proofs for tawhid as Ibrahim's religion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an establishes tawhid as the foundational creed of Prophet Ibrahim and all the prophets after him.

Core Idea
Tawhid is the unchanging religion of all prophets from Ibrahim to Muhammad.

Imam Ghazali opens this chapter by grounding the creed of tawhid in the example of Prophet Ibrahim and his descendants. The Qur'anic verses he cites show that submission to the one true God was the central message passed down through the prophetic lineage. This passage establishes that tawhid is not a later innovation but the original religion of Ibrahim, which every prophet preached and embodied.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses about Ibrahim
Read the opening verses where Ibrahim is commanded to submit, and he does, and he enjoins his children to die as Muslims. Notice that submission (islam) is the core of tawhid.
The phrase 'أسلمت لرب العالمين' is a direct declaration of monotheistic submission.
2
Observe Ya'qub's sons' testimony
Read the verses about Ya'qub's deathbed and his sons' response. They affirm worship of one God, showing continuity of tawhid through generations.
3
Understand the prophets' role
The author then states that prophets are the first commanded to believe in tawhid. Read the verses commanding the Prophet Muhammad to be among the submitters and to avoid shirk.
This reverses the common assumption; prophets are not exempt but are the foremost believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن يرغب عن ملة إبراهيم إلا من سفه نفسه , ولقد اصطفيناه في الدنيا , وانه في الآخرة لمن الصالحين , إذ قال له ربه أسلم , قال : أسلمت لرب العالمين ووصى بها إبراهيم بنيه , ويعقوب يا بني إن الله اصطفى لكم الدين فلا تموتن إلا وأنتم مسلمون, أم كنتم شهداء إذ حضر يعقوب الموت إذ قال لبنيه : ما تعبدون من بعدي ؟ قالوا : نعبد إلاهك وإلاه آبائك إبراهيم واسماعيل واسحاق إلاها واحدا ونحن له مسلمون . وَاتَّبَعْتُ مِلَّةَ آبَائِي إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ , مَا كَانَ لَنَا أَن تُشْرِكَ بِالله مِن شَيْءٍ ) (۱) والذين يختارهم الله لتبليغ أديانه إلى الناس وبيانها لهم , وتطبيقها على حياتهم , وهم الأنبياء والرسل , هم أول من يؤمر بالإيمان بعقيدة التوحيد , وتفهم حقيقتها : قُلْ إِنِّي أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أَكُونَ أَوَّلَ مَنْ أَسْلَمَ , وَلَا تَكُونَنَّ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ ) (۲) قُلْ إِنَّمَا أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أَعْبُدَ اللَّهَ وَلَا أَشْرِكَ به , إلَيْهِ أَدْعُوا , وَإِلَيْهِ مَآب ) (۳) قُلْ أَفَغَيْرَ اللهِ تَأْمُرُونِي أَعْبُدُ أَيُّهَا الْجَاهِلُونَ , وَلَقَدْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْكَ وإلَى الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكَ , لَئِنْ أَشْرَكْتَ لَيَحْبَطَنَّ عَمَلُكَ وَلَتَكُونَنَّ مِنَ الْخَاسِرِينَ , بَلِ اللَّهَ فَاعْبُدْ وَكُن من الشَّاكِرِينَ ) (٤) . (۱) آية (۳۸) سورة يوسف (۱۲) . (۲) آية (١٤) سورة الأنعام (٦) . (۳) آية (٣٦) سورة الرعد (١١٣) (٤) آية (٦٤ - ٦٦) سورة الزمر (٣٩)
And who turns away from the religion of Ibrahim except one who fools himself? And indeed We chose him in this world, and indeed in the Hereafter he will be among the righteous. When his Lord said to him: 'Submit,' he said: 'I have submitted to the Lord of the worlds.' And Ibrahim enjoined it upon his sons, and [so did] Ya'qub: 'O my sons, indeed Allah has chosen for you the religion, so do not die except as Muslims.' Or were you witnesses when death approached Ya'qub, when he said to his sons: 'What will you worship after me?' They said: 'We will worship your God and the God of your fathers, Ibrahim, Isma'il, and Ishaq, one God, and we are to Him submissive.' (1) 'And I have followed the religion of my fathers, Ibrahim, Ishaq, and Ya'qub; it was not for us to associate anything with Allah.' (1) And those whom Allah chooses to convey His religions to the people, to explain them to them, and to implement them in their lives—and they are the prophets and messengers—they are the first to be commanded to believe in the creed of tawhid (monotheism) and to understand its reality: Say: 'Indeed, I have been commanded to be the first of those who submit, and never be among the polytheists.' (2) Say: 'I am only commanded to worship Allah and not associate partners with Him; to Him I call, and to Him is my return.' (3) Say: 'Do you order me to worship other than Allah, O ignorant ones? And it has been revealed to you and to those before you: If you associate partners with Allah, your deeds will surely become worthless, and you will surely be among the losers. Rather, worship Allah and be among the grateful.' (4) (1) Surah Yusuf, verse 38. (2) Surah al-An'am, verse 14. (3) Surah ar-Ra'd, verse 36. (4) Surah az-Zumar, verses 64-66.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof that the religion of monotheism (tawhid) is the core of the message of all prophets, starting with Ibrahim. The author begins by quoting Quranic verses that show Ibrahim's submission and his exhortation to his children to die as Muslims, and the response of Ya'qub's sons affirming worship of one God. The author then draws the lesson: the prophets and messengers are the first to be commanded to believe in this creed and to understand it fully. The verses quoted (Q 6:14, 13:36, 39:64-66) all command the Prophet Muhammad to be the first to submit and to reject shirk, and they warn that associating partners with Allah nullifies deeds. The author is establishing that tawhid is the foundation of all divine messages and that prophets are the foremost in adhering to it.

Key Terms
عقيدة التوحيد
ملة إبراهيم
الأنبياء والرسل
أسلم
المشركين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that prophets were not required to believe in tawhid themselves.
Correction: This passage explicitly states that prophets are the first to be commanded to believe in tawhid and to understand its reality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who are the first to be commanded to believe in the creed of tawhid?
A) The common people
B) The prophets and messengers
C) The scholars
D) The angels

Key Takeaway
The creed of tawhid is the consistent message of all prophets, starting with Ibrahim, and every prophet is the first to believe and act upon it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you die as a Muslim (someone who has submitted fully to Allah)? What area of your life have you not yet submitted to Him, and what is one concrete step you will take today to surrender that area?
?
The Prophet was commanded to be the first to submit and to reject shirk. Is there any hidden 'association' in your heart—like seeking praise, fearing people's opinions, or relying on your own plans more than Allah's will—that you need to tear down today? Name it specifically and decide how to uproot it.
?
Ibrahim taught his children to worship one God and to die in a state of submission. If your children (or those you influence) were asked what you truly worship, would they say 'Allah alone' or would they see you prioritizing worldly things? What change in your daily routine would make your devotion unmistakable?

The Pure Tawheed of Islam
Quranic command to worship Allah alone and the Prophet's role in purifying tawheed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the centrality of pure tawheed in Islam and how the Prophet's teaching distanced it from shirk and tashbih.

Core Idea
Pure tawheed means exclusive worship of Allah, far from shirk and anthropomorphism.

Islam's fundamental call is to worship Allah alone and to avoid associating partners with Him. The Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) embodied this teaching and conveyed it with utmost clarity, removing any confusion about the nature of divinity. In this lesson, we explore the Quranic foundation of tawheed and its perfect expression through the Prophet's mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Begin by reading the two Quranic verses quoted at the start of the passage. Notice the command to worship Allah alone and the warning against shirk.
The verses are from Surah An-Nisa (4:36 and 4:48).
2
Understand the Prophet's role
The passage says the Prophet's personal practice and his teaching reached the utmost purity of tawheed. Reflect on how he distanced believers from shirk and tashbih.
3
Connect to core idea
Ask yourself: Why is tawheed the foundation of Islam? The passage shows that proper understanding of divinity requires keeping it far from human attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْبُدُوا اللهَ وَلَا تُشْرِكُوا بِهِ شَيْئاً (إِنَّ اللهَ لا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ). فكان ما أمر به، عليه الصلاة والسلام، في نفسه، وما أمر بتبليغه للناس صورة بلغت الغاية القصوى في صفاء التوحيد ونقائه، والعبد به عن شوائب الشرك وعوارض التشبيه، وفهم الألوهية وتقديرها حق قدرها، وإنزالها منزلتها، بعيدة عن البشرية وعوارضها.
وسيدنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، حين انتدب لتبليغ رسالة الإسلام التي تحتل منها حقيقة التوحيد هذه المكانة، قد حددت حقيقته، وبشريته، فالقرآن قد عنى في كل مناسبة بأن يزيل كل لبس أو اشتباه من شأنه أن يعلق بحقيقة الألوهية أو بحقيقة النبوة، فيسيء الناس فهمهما، أو يسيئون فهم حقيقة التوحيد الذي هو أساس الإسلام.
ومن هنا كانت بشرية [الرسول ل الله موضوعا عنى القرآن ببيانه وتأكيده؟] فرسول الاسلام ولد وعاش تحت أعين التاريخ وسمعه، معروف الأب والأم والأسرة، ومعروف الشرف والكرامة بين قومه، وحياته ليست ظلالا يكتنفها الابهام، ويخفى قسماتها الغموض، بل هى تاريخ حقيقي واضح المعالم، لا مجال فيه للخيال والتفسير والتأويل.
وقد حظيت حياته صلوات الله وسلامه عليه من المسلمين الأول بالعناية البالغة، فدونوا دقائقها وتفاصيلها بصورة لم تحظ بها حياة نبي من الأنبياء قبله.
And worship Allah and do not associate anything with Him. Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills. So what he (peace and blessings be upon him) was commanded in himself and what he was commanded to convey to people became a form that reached the utmost degree in the purity of tawheed and its cleanness, and the servant's distance from the impurities of shirk and the accidents of tashbih, and understanding of divinity and its estimation rightfully, and placing it in its proper station, far from human qualities and their accidents. And our master, the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, when he was commissioned to convey the message of Islam, in which the reality of tawheed occupies this position, his reality and his humanity were clearly defined. So the Qur'an took care on every occasion to remove any confusion or ambiguity that might attach to the reality of divinity or the reality of prophethood, causing people to misunderstand them, or to misunderstand the reality of tawheed which is the foundation of Islam. Hence, the humanity of [the Messenger of Allah was a subject that the Qur'an intended to clarify and emphasize?] For the Messenger of Islam was born and lived under the eyes of history and its hearing, known by father, mother, and family, known for honor and dignity among his people. His life is not a shadow enveloped by ambiguity, nor are its features hidden by obscurity, but rather it is a real history with clear outlines, with no room for imagination, interpretation, or allegory. And his life, may the blessings of Allah and peace be upon him, received the utmost attention from the early Muslims, as they recorded its details and particulars in a manner that no life of any prophet before him received.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage clarifies the central place of pure tawheed in Islam and emphasizes the historical humanity of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). It begins by quoting two Quranic verses (4:36 and 4:48) that command exclusive worship of Allah and warn against shirk. The author then explains that the Prophet's own practice and his teaching achieved the utmost purity of tawheed, distancing believers from shirk and tashbih (anthropomorphism). The Qur'an consistently removed any confusion about the nature of divinity and prophethood, ensuring correct understanding of tawheed as the foundation of Islam. The humanity of the Prophet is a key point: he was a real historical figure with known lineage, born and lived under the scrutiny of history, unlike legendary figures. His life was meticulously documented by the early Muslims, more so than any previous prophet. This establishes the credibility and clarity of his message and refutes any doubts about his prophethood being based on myth or ambiguity.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الشرك
التشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that tawheed is merely believing in one God, without needing to actively avoid shirk and tashbih.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that tawheed requires not only belief but also purification from all forms of shirk and anthropomorphism, as shown by the Prophet's teaching.

Checkpoint
What are the two Quranic themes emphasized by the author in the opening?
A) Worship Allah and associate partners with Him
B) Worship Allah alone and avoid shirk
C) Worship many gods and ask forgiveness for all
D) Worship only through the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Tawheed is not just belief but a pure devotion to Allah, free from shirk and anthropomorphism, as perfectly taught by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, where do you find yourself subtly attributing human qualities to Allah, even in your thoughts? How can you actively purify your tawheed from such tashbih?
?
When you face difficulty, do you instinctively seek help from other than Allah? The passage says worship Allah alone and don't associate anything. Reflect on one area where you might be relying on creation more than the Creator. What step will you take to change?
?
The Prophet's teaching reached the utmost purity in tawheed. Are you content with your current understanding of Allah's divinity, or do you strive to purify it further? Commit to one action to deepen your tawheed.

The Prophet's Humanity and Historical Evidence
The Prophet's humanity is clearly defined and historically documented to prevent confusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an and early Muslim documentation emphasize the historical humanity of the Prophet Muhammad (pbuh) to clarify the nature of prophethood and prevent confusion with divinity.

Core Idea
The Prophet's humanity is historically documented, removing myth and confusion about prophethood.

The Qur'an repeatedly stresses that Prophet Muhammad was a human being, with a real life and known lineage. This clarity is essential to prevent people from confusing the nature of prophethood with divinity. The early Muslims meticulously recorded his life, providing a solid historical foundation that distinguishes Islam from legend.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Prophet's humanity
Focus on the part beginning with 'Our master, the Messenger of Allah...' Notice how the Qur'an is said to remove confusions about divinity and prophethood.
2
Identify the historical details
The passage lists that the Prophet was born under history's eye, known by family, and lived a clear life. List these details.
This shows his life is real, not mythical.
3
Appreciate the documentation
The passage says early Muslims recorded his life in detail, more than any previous prophet. Reflect on how this strengthens the credibility of his message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that emphasizing the Prophet's humanity reduces his status or suggests he was an ordinary man without divine support.
Correction: The passage shows that his clear humanity actually strengthens the evidence for his prophethood by making his life verifiable and removing confusion with divinity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how did the Qur'an treat the Prophet's humanity?
A) It ignored it
B) It emphasized it to remove confusion
C) It denied it
D) It made it ambiguous

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's humanity is a historical fact, clearly documented, which prevents confusion between the divine and the prophetic and validates his message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's life is so clearly documented, what specific doubt about his message still lingers in your heart? Confront that doubt with the historical evidence mentioned in this lesson and write down what you conclude.
?
The early Muslims recorded every detail of the Prophet's life. Does your own life reflect that kind of devotion to following his example? What is one area where you know his sunnah but have not implemented it? What will you change today?
?
Knowing that the Qur'an deliberately clarifies the Prophet's humanity, how does this make his role as your role model more relatable? In what way have you been distant from him because you thought he was too perfect? How will you draw closer to him now?

The Threefold Oneness: Foundation of Tawhid
Imam Ghazali enumerates the three kinds of oneness that constitute tawhid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tawhid is built on three inseparable aspects: Allah's oneness in dominion, essence, and worship.

Core Idea
Tawhid rests on three pillars: sole dominion, unique essence, exclusive worship.

Imam Ghazali begins by linking the testimony of faith to the concept of tawhid, explaining why Islam is called the religion of tawhid. He then breaks down tawhid into three fundamental kinds of oneness that are inseparable in the message of all prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the three kinds of oneness
Identify the three ways Allah is described as One: in His dominion and actions, in His essence and attributes, and in His divinity and worship.
Notice the Arabic terms: ملكه وأفعاله, ذاته وصفاته, ألوهيته وعبادته.
2
Understand the inseparability
The author emphasizes that these three types are never separate in prophetic tawhid. Ask yourself why all three are necessary.
This prepares us for the later distinction between rububiyyah and uluhiyyah.
3
Connect to the shahada
Reflect on how the testimony 'La ilaha illallah' encompasses all three kinds of oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفهم طبيعة الرسالة والرسل على هذا النحو من الوساطة، يسلمنا إلى الحديث عن التوحيد الذي تقرره القاعدة الأولى التي نحن بصدد الحديث عنها وهي: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله. والذي سمي دين الإسلام من أجلها توحيدا، لأن مبناه على أن الله تعالى واحد في ملكه وأفعاله، لا شريك له، وواحد في ذاته وصفاته لا نظير له، وواحد في ألوهيته وعبادته لا ند له. وإلى هذه الأنواع الثلاثة ينقسم توحيد الأنبياء والمرسلين الذين جاءوا به من عند الله سبحانه، وهي متلازمة، كل نوع منها لا ينفك عن الآخر، فمن أتى بنوع منها ولم يأت بالآخر، فما ذاك إلا لأنه لم يأت به على وجه الكمال المطلوب. والتوحيد: الذي تقرره وقررته القاعدة الأولى وهي: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله نوعان: توحيد في المعرفة والإثبات: وهو توحيد الربوبية والأسماء والصفات. وتوحيد في الطلب والمقصد: وهو توحيد الإلهية والعبادة. والنوع الأول: توحيد الربوبية والملك، وهو الإقرار بأن الله تعالى رب كل شيء ومالكه، وخالقه ورازقه، وأنه المحيي المميت، النافع الضار، المتفرد بإجابة الدعاء عند الاضطرار، الذي له الأمر كله، وبيده الخير كله، القادر على ما يشاء، ليس له في ذلك شريك، ويدخل في ذلك الإيمان بالقدر. وهذا التوحيد لا يكفي العبد في حصول الإسلام، بل لا بد أن يأتي مع ذلك بلازمه من توحيد الإلهية، لأن الله تعالى حكى عن المشركين أنهم مقرون بهذا التوحيد لله وحده: قال تعالى: (قُلْ مَن يَرْزُقُكُم مِّنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ، أَمَن يَمْلِكُ السَّمْعَ وَالْأَبْصَارَ، وَمَن يُخْرِجُ الْحَيَّ مِنَ الْمَيِّتِ وَيُخْرِجُ الْمَيِّتَ مِنَ الْحَيِّ، وَمَن يُدَبِّرُ الْأَمْرَ فَسَيَقُولُونَ اللهُ، فَقُلْ أَفَلَا تَتَّقُونَ) (١) وقال تعالى: (وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُم مَّنْ خَلَقَهُمْ لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ) (۲) وقال سبحانه: (وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُم مِّن نَّزَّلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ مِن بَعْدِ مَوْتِهَا، لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ) (۳) وقال تعالى: (أَمَّن يُجِيبُ الْمُضْطَرَّ إِذَا دَعَاهُ وَيَكْشِفُ السُّوءَ وَيَجْعَلُكُمْ خُلَفَاءَ الْأَرْضِ، أَإِلٰهٌ مَّعَ اللَّهِ قَلِيلًا مَّا تَذَكَّرُونَ) (٤) فهم كانوا يعلمون أن جميع ذلك لله وحده، ولم يكونوا بذلك مسلمين، بل قال تعالى: (وَمَا يُؤْمِنُ أَكْثَرُهُم بِاللّٰهِ إِلَّا وَهُم مُّشْرِكُونَ) (٥) يقول مجاهد رضي الله عنه في معنى الآية: إيمانهم بالله قولهم: إنَّ الله خلقنا ويرزقنا ويميتنا، فهذا إيمان مع شرك.
And understanding the nature of the message and the messengers in this manner of mediation leads us to talk about tawhid, which is established by the first principle that we are discussing, namely: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. And the religion of Islam was named tawhid because of it, because its foundation is that Allah Almighty is One in His dominion and His actions, no partner to Him; and One in His essence and attributes, no likeness to Him; and One in His divinity and worship, no rival to Him. And the tawhid of the prophets and messengers who brought it from Allah Almighty is divided into these three types, and they are inseparable; each type is not detached from the other. Whoever brings one type without the other, that is only because he did not bring it with the required perfection. And tawhid, which is established and was established by the first principle, namely: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, is of two types: tawhid of knowledge and affirmation, which is tawhid of lordship (rububiyyah) and names and attributes; and tawhid of intent and purpose, which is tawhid of divinity (uluhiyyah) and worship. And the first type: tawhid of lordship and dominion, which is the acknowledgment that Allah Almighty is the Lord of everything and its Owner, its Creator and Provider, and that He is the One who gives life and causes death, the Benefactor and the Harmer, the Unique in answering the prayer of the distressed, to Whom belongs all command, in Whose hand is all good, the Omnipotent over whatever He wills, having no partner in that; and faith in predestination (qadar) enters into that. And this tawhid is not sufficient for the servant to attain Islam; rather, he must bring along with it its necessary consequence of tawhid of divinity, because Allah Almighty related that the polytheists acknowledged this tawhid for Allah alone. He said, the Most High: 'Say: Who provides for you from the sky and the earth? Or who owns hearing and sight? And who brings forth the living from the dead and brings forth the dead from the living? And who arranges the affair? They will say: Allah. Then say: Will you not then fear?' (1) And He said, the Most High: 'And if you ask them who created them, they will surely say: Allah.' (2) And He said, the Exalted: 'And if you ask them who sends down rain from the sky and revives the earth after its death, they will surely say: Allah.' (3) And He said, the Most High: 'Is He [not best] who responds to the distressed one when he calls upon Him and removes the evil and makes you successors of the earth? Is there a god with Allah? Little do you remember.' (4) So they knew that all of that belongs to Allah alone, but they were not thereby Muslims. Rather, He said, the Most High: 'And most of them do not believe in Allah except while they are polytheists.' (5) Mujahid, may Allah be pleased with him, said regarding the meaning of the verse: 'Their belief in Allah is their saying: Indeed Allah created us and provides for us and causes us to die; so this is belief along with polytheism.'
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies tawhid into two essential types, demonstrating the insufficiency of acknowledging only Allah's lordship (rububiyyah) without worshipping Him alone (uluhiyyah). The author begins by connecting the understanding of prophethood to the fundamental testimony of faith, from which tawhid derives its name. He explains that Islam is called "tawhid" because it is built upon three kinds of oneness: oneness of dominion and actions, oneness of essence and attributes, and oneness of divinity and worship. These three are inseparable in the tawhid brought by the prophets. The author then states that the testimony 'La ilaha illallah' establishes two types of tawhid: (1) tawhid of knowledge and affirmation, which encompasses rububiyyah and names/attributes, and (2) tawhid of intent and purpose, which is uluhiyyah and worship. He elaborates on the first type as acknowledging Allah as the sole Lord, Owner, Creator, Provider, etc., and notes that faith in qadar is included. Crucially, he asserts that this first type alone is insufficient for Islam; the second type—worship of Allah alone—must accompany it. To prove this, he cites four Quranic verses showing that the polytheists acknowledged Allah's exclusive lordship over creation, provision, life and death, and response to distress, yet they were not Muslims. Finally, he quotes Mujahid's tafsir that their 'belief' in Allah as Creator and Provider was accompanied by shirk. Thus, true tawhid requires both recognition of Allah's sole lordship and exclusive worship of Him.

Key Terms
توحيد
واحد في ملكه وأفعاله
واحد في ذاته وصفاته
واحد في ألوهيته وعبادته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Islam called the religion of tawhid?
A) Because it was founded by a prophet named Tawhid.
B) Because its foundation is the oneness of Allah in three aspects.
C) Because it emphasizes tawhid al-rububiyyah only.
D) Because it rejects the three kinds of oneness.

Key Takeaway
The tawhid brought by all prophets encompasses three inseparable types of oneness: in Allah's dominion, in His essence and attributes, and in His divinity and worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'La ilaha illallah', do you truly feel that every part of your life—your work, relationships, and inner desires—is governed by Allah's sole dominion, unique essence, and exclusive right to worship? Where do you find the most resistance?
?
Think of a moment you obeyed your own desire over Allah's command. Which of the three onenesses were you violating in that moment—His lordship over your actions, His unique right to be obeyed, or both? What will you change today?
?
The prophets brought all three types of tawhid as inseparable. Is your faith complete, or are you comfortable with only believing in Allah's lordship while neglecting His exclusive right to your worship? Name one idol in your heart you must destroy.

Allah's Existence
beginner
7 min
The Two Types of Tawhid and the Insufficiency of Rububiyyah
Imam Ghazali classifies tawhid into two types and proves the necessity of uluhiyyah with Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between tawhid of lordship (rububiyyah) and tawhid of worship (uluhiyyah), and why acknowledging Allah as Lord alone is not enough to be a Muslim.

Core Idea
True tawhid requires not only believing in Allah as the sole Lord but also worshipping Him alone.

Having established the threefold foundation, Imam Ghazali now presents the two main categories of tawhid derived from the shahada. He explains tawhid of rububiyyah in detail and proves from the Quran that the polytheists affirmed this but were not Muslims, because they failed to adopt tawhid of uluhiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of tawhid
The passage divides tawhid into two types related to the shahada. Find and note them: tawhid of knowledge/affirmation and tawhid of intent/purpose.
The first includes rububiyyah and names/attributes; the second is uluhiyyah and worship.
2
Examine the definition of rububiyyah
Read the detailed description of tawhid of lordship and dominion. List the attributes mentioned: Lord, Owner, Creator, Provider, etc.
Also note that belief in qadar is included here.
3
Study the Quranic proof
The author cites four verses showing that the polytheists acknowledged Allah's sole lordship. Reflect on why this acknowledgment did not make them Muslims.
The key is in the verse: 'And most of them do not believe in Allah except while they are polytheists.'

The author begins by connecting the understanding of prophethood to the fundamental testimony of faith, from which tawhid derives its name. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that believing in Allah as the Creator and Provider (tawhid al-rububiyyah) is enough to be a Muslim.
Correction: The passage shows that the polytheists also believed in Allah's sole lordship, yet they were not Muslims because they worshipped others besides Allah. True Islam requires both rububiyyah and uluhiyyah.

Checkpoint
Why is tawhid of rububiyyah alone insufficient for Islam according to this passage?
A) Because the polytheists acknowledged Allah as Lord, Provider, and Creator, yet they were not Muslims.
B) Because tawhid of rububiyyah is not mentioned in the Quran.
C) Because it only applies to prophets.
D) Because it contradicts the concept of qadar.

Key Takeaway
Tawhid of lordship (rububiyyah) is necessary but insufficient; tawhid of worship (uluhiyyah) is essential for true Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that simply believing in Allah's existence and lordship is enough for your salvation? After reading this passage, what specific area of your worship might you be neglecting that could be considered shirk?
?
The polytheists knew Allah was their Creator and Provider, yet they worshipped others. In your daily life, are you doing things that, while you affirm Allah's lordship, you still seek the approval or help of others as if they are independent sources? How can you shift your reliance entirely to Allah?
?
This passage confronts the comfortable idea that 'I believe in God' is sufficient. If you were to honestly evaluate your life, is your tawhid of uluhiyyah (worship) as strong as your tawhid of rububiyyah (belief)? What is one concrete step you can take today to strengthen your worship of Allah alone?

The Kuffar's Recognition of Lordship but Shirk in Worship
Argument about shirk in worship among pre-Islamic Arabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the pre-Islamic Arabs were declared disbelievers despite acknowledging Allah's lordship, and the central importance of tawheed al-uluhiyyah.

Core Idea
Acknowledging Allah's lordship is not enough; true faith requires exclusive worship.

The passage presents a critical distinction between tawheed ar-rububiyyah and tawheed al-uluhiyyah. The pre-Islamic Arabs acknowledged Allah's creation and sovereignty, yet the Quran condemned them as polytheists. This lesson explores the decisive factor that necessitated jihad against them, rooted in the meaning of la ilaha illa Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the structure: it first states what the kuffar knew, then describes their worship, then asks a question and answers it.
The passage is a clear argument from historical facts.
2
Identify the kuffar's beliefs
List the things the pre-Islamic Arabs acknowledged about Allah and the acts of worship they performed. Also note their claim to follow Ibrahim.
They believed in resurrection and predestination too.
3
Find the central question and answer
The author asks what justified fighting them despite this knowledge. Find that sentence and the answer: their shirk in tawheed of worship.
This is the key point of the lesson.
4
Reflect on the meaning of la ilaha illa Allah
Consider how this passage shows that the shahada is not just about affirming existence but about exclusive devotion in worship.
This connects to the core idea.

فتبين أن الكفار يعرفون الله تعالى ويعرفون ربوبيته ، وملكه وقهره ، وكانوا مع ذلك يعبدونه ويخلصون له أنواعا من العبادات ، كالحج ، والصدقة ، والدعاء ، وقت الاضطرار ونحو ذلك ، ويدعون أنهم على ملة سيدنا ابراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، فأنزل الله تعالى : مَا كَانَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ يَهُودِيًا وَلا نَصُرَانّياً ولَكن كَانَ حَنِيفاً مُسلِماً وَمَا كَانَ مِنَ المُشْرِكِينَ . فكان بعضهم يؤمن بالبعث والحساب ، وبعضهم يؤمن بالقدر ، ومثل هذا كان يوجد في عقائدهم . فوجب على كل من عقل عن الله تعالى أن ينظر ويبحث عن السبب الذي أوجب سفك دمائهم ويسبي نسائهم وإباحة أموالهم مع هذا الإقرار والمعرفة ، وما ذاك إلا لاشراكهم في توحيد العبادة الذي هو معنى : « لا إله إلا الله .
So it became clear that the disbelievers know Allah Almighty and know His lordship, His dominion, and His subjugation, and yet with that they used to worship Him and devote to Him types of worship, like Hajj, charity, supplication at times of distress and the like, and they claimed to be upon the religion of our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him. Then Allah Almighty revealed: 'Ibrahim was neither a Jew nor a Christian, but he was a hanif, a Muslim, and he was not of the polytheists.' Some of them believed in resurrection and reckoning, and some believed in predestination, and similar things existed in their beliefs. So it is incumbent upon everyone who understands from Allah Almighty to consider and seek the reason that necessitated shedding their blood, capturing their women, and permitting their wealth, despite this acknowledgment and knowledge. And that is nothing other than their association in the tawheed of worship which is the meaning of 'la ilaha illa Allah'.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a historical-theological argument about the pre-Islamic Arabs (mushrikeen). The author demonstrates that the polytheists of the Quraysh and others did not deny Allah's existence, lordship, or many of His attributes. They acknowledged His creation, sustenance, and sovereignty. Moreover, they performed acts of worship directed to Allah — such as pilgrimage, charity, and earnest supplication during crises. They also claimed to follow the religion of Ibrahim. Yet Allah revealed that Ibrahim was not a polytheist; he was a hanif and Muslim, thus separating their practice from his. Some of them even believed in the afterlife and divine decree. Despite all this, Allah permitted fighting them, taking spoils, and captivity. The author poses the question: what was the decisive reason? The answer is that they committed shirk in 'tawheed of worship' (tawheed al-uluhiyyah), which is the essence of la ilaha illa Allah. This shows that mere acknowledgment of Allah's lordship is not enough; what distinguishes true Islam from shirk is exclusive devotion in worship.

Key Terms
توحيد العبادة
لا إله إلا الله
الربوبية
الإشراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Pre-Islamic Arabs were atheists or denied Allah completely.
Correction: They acknowledged Allah's lordship and performed worship, but their shirk was in directing worship to others alongside Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main reason for fighting the kuffar despite their recognition of Allah's lordship?
A) Their denial of resurrection
B) Their disbelief in predestination
C) Their shirk in tawheed of worship
D) Their abandonment of pilgrimage

Key Takeaway
The decisive factor in declaring someone a polytheist is not the denial of Allah's existence but the association of partners in worship, which is the core of la ilaha illa Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know Allah is your Lord—you say 'Rabb' and 'Malik'—but where in your daily life do you still seek approval from people more than from Him? Are there prayers you rush through, but careers you perfect? That is the very gap this passage exposes.
?
The disbelievers did Hajj, gave charity, and cried to Allah in distress—yet they were still polytheists. Now look at your own heart: are there acts of worship you perform, thinking they make you Muslim, while you cherish something else alongside Allah? What would that be?
?
Allah permitted the shedding of their blood despite their knowledge. Pause: if your life were examined right now, would the decisive factor be that you knew Allah, or that you worshipped Him alone without any shadow of shirk? What needs to change today for that answer to be clear?

Essential Beliefs in God
Ghazali lists beliefs about God whose negation invalidates Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core beliefs about God that are necessary for being a Muslim, including His existence, oneness, transcendence, and sole right to worship.

Core Idea
Negating any essential belief about God invalidates one's Islam entirely.

Ghazali begins by stating the non-negotiable fundamentals of faith. These are not optional niceties; they are the boundary markers of Islam. Denial of any one of them places a person outside the fold. This lesson covers the beliefs concerning Allah Himself: His existence, His oneness, His transcendence above all imperfections, and His exclusive right to be worshipped.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text from 'فمن لم يؤمن بوجود الله' to 'واستباح عبادة مخلوق ما من المخلوقات'. Notice the repeated conditional 'لم يؤمن' which sets the logical structure.
The passage uses a legalistic style: if-then.
2
Identify each required belief
List the beliefs about God that Ghazali mentions: existence, oneness, transcendence (from resemblance, incarnation, union), sole management of the universe, and exclusive right to worship.
Each of these is a separate condition for being Muslim.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: why does Ghazali include transcendence and management? What errors do these guard against?
Incarnation (hulul) and union (ittihad) were claimed by some extreme groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن لم يؤمن بوجود الله سبحانه ، أو لم يؤمن بوحدانيته تعالى ، وتنزهه عن المشابهة ، والحلول والاتحاد ، أو لم يؤمن بتفرده بتدبير الكون والتصرف فيه ، واستحقاق العبادة والتقديس ، واستباح عبادة مخلوق ما من المخلوقات ، لم يؤمن بأن الله رسالات إلى خلقه ، بعث بها رسله صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم ، وأنزل عليهم كتبه عن طريق ملائكته ، أو لم يؤمن بما تضمنته الكتب من الرسل ، أو فرق بين الرسل الذين قص علينا ، فآمن بالبعض وكفر بالبعض ، أو لم يؤمن بأن الحياة الدنيا تفنى ويعقبها دار أخرى هي دار الاقامة الأبدية ، بل اعتقد أن الحياة الدنيا حياة دائمة لا الجزاء دار تنقطع ، أو اعتقد أنها تفنى فناء دائما لا بعث بعده ، ولا حساب ولا جزاء ، أو لم يؤمن بأن أصول شرع الله تعالى فيما حرم ، وفيما أوجب ، هي دينه القويم الذي يجب أن يتبع ، فحرم من تلقاء نفسه ما رأى تحريمه ، وأوجب من تلقاء نفسه ما رأى وجوبه من لم يؤمن بجانب من هذه الحقائق لا يكون مسلما ، ولا تجرى عليه أحكام المسلمين . وعليه فما أحدثه المتكلمون من تفسير وسؤال وتوجيه اشكال ، ثم اشتغالهم بحل ذلك كله ، فهو بدعة ، وضرره في حق عموم
So whoever does not believe in the existence of God Almighty, or does not believe in His oneness, His transcendence above resemblance, incarnation and union, or does not believe in His unique management of the universe and disposal therein, and His deserving worship and sanctification, and permits worship of any created being among the creations, does not believe that God has messages to His creation, sent by His messengers, peace be upon them, and sent down books to them by way of His angels, or does not believe in what the books contain from the messengers, or makes a distinction between the messengers who are narrated to us, believing in some and disbelieving in others, or does not believe that the worldly life will perish and be followed by another abode which is the abode of everlasting residence, but rather believes that the worldly life is a permanent life with no recompense, an abode that ceases, or believes that it perishes an eternal perishing with no resurrection after it, no reckoning and no recompense, or does not believe that the principles of God's law concerning what is forbidden and what is obligatory are His straight religion which must be followed, so he forbids on his own authority what he deems forbidden, and obligates on his own authority what he deems obligatory. Whoever does not believe in any aspect of these truths is not a Muslim, and the rulings of Muslims are not applied to him. Accordingly, what the mutakallimun have innovated of interpretation, question, direction of doubt, and then their occupation with solving all that, it is innovation, and its harm is upon the general public.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive statement of the essential beliefs of Islam, the negation of any of which renders one outside the fold of Islam. Ghazali lists the necessary beliefs: 1) Existence of God, 2) His oneness and transcendence above anthropomorphism, incarnation, and union, 3) His sole disposal of the universe and right to worship, 4) That God sent messages and messengers, revealed books via angels, 5) Belief in the content of the books and messengers, without distinguishing between them, 6) Belief in the afterlife: that the world will end and be followed by an eternal abode, rejecting both eternal worldliness and annihilation without resurrection, 7) That the principles of Sharia (halal and haram) are God's religion and must be followed, not based on personal opinion. Whoever fails in any of these is not Muslim. After establishing these necessary beliefs, Ghazali critiques the mutakallimun (theologians) who have innovated excessive interpretation, questioning, and the raising and solving of doubts, calling it bid'ah and harmful to the general public. This critique aligns with Ghazali's concern about the dangers of speculative theology for the masses.

Key Terms
وجود الله
وحدانية
تنزه
تدبير الكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person can believe in God's existence but deny His oneness and still be Muslim.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly says that denying any of these beliefs, including oneness, removes one from Islam.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the ruling on a person who believes in God's existence but permits worshipping a saint?
A) He is still a Muslim.
B) He is a Muslim but sinful.
C) He is not a Muslim.
D) He is a hypocrite.

Key Takeaway
Islamic faith requires belief in God's existence, oneness, transcendence, sole management, and exclusive right to worship; denying any of these nullifies Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you caught yourself mentally picturing God in a certain way, even briefly? How does Ghazali's negation of 'resemblance, incarnation, and union' challenge you to purify your concept of God right now, and what step will you take today to repent from such thoughts?
?
Is there any created being, desire, or goal in your life that you treat as worthy of ultimate devotion—more than God? If so, how does this passage's warning about 'permitting worship of any created being' expose that hidden idol, and what concrete action will you take before your next prayer to tear it down?
?
Have you ever secretly doubted God's management of your life when things didn't go your way? How does the belief that God alone manages the universe demand that you surrender your plans to Him this very hour, and what would that surrender look like in practice?

Belief in Prophets and Books
Ghazali states that denying any aspect of prophethood invalidates Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the necessity of believing in all prophets and divine books without discrimination.

Core Idea
Islam requires belief in all messengers and books; making distinctions is disbelief.

After establishing beliefs about God, Ghazali turns to prophethood. A Muslim must believe that God sent messengers, revealed books through angels, and that these books contain guidance. Crucially, one must believe in all messengers without singling out some for rejection. This lesson covers that essential aspect of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic from 'لم يؤمن بأن الله رسالات' to 'فآمن بالبعض وكفر بالبعض'. Note the negation conditions.
2
Identify the components
List the sub-beliefs: God sent messages, messengers, books via angels, belief in the content, and belief in all messengers equally.
3
Understand why discrimination is problematic
Think about the Jewish and Christian claims that they accept some prophets and reject others (e.g., Muhammad). Ghazali's statement addresses that.

Belief in the Afterlife and Sharia
Ghazali states that denying the afterlife or the divine origin of Sharia invalidates Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the necessity of belief in the afterlife and adherence to the revealed principles of Sharia.

Core Idea
Denying the afterlife or replacing Sharia with personal opinion removes one from Islam.

Ghazali completes his list of essential beliefs by addressing two crucial areas: the afterlife and the principles of divine law. One must believe that this world will end and be followed by an eternal abode of recompense, and that the rules of halal and haram are set by God alone. Rejecting either means losing the status of being Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read from 'أو لم يؤمن بأن الحياة الدنيا تفنى' to 'من لم يؤمن بجانب من هذه الحقائق لا يكون مسلما'. Notice the two main topics: afterlife and Sharia.
2
Identify the sub-beliefs about the afterlife
List: this world will perish, it will be followed by an eternal abode, and there is resurrection, reckoning, and recompense.
Ghazali also negates two false beliefs: world is eternal, or it ends permanently with no resurrection.
3
Identify the belief about Sharia
One must accept that the principles of Sharia (what is obligatory and forbidden) are from God and must be followed, not based on personal opinion.

Critique of Innovated Theology
Ghazali criticizes innovative theological practices as harmful to the masses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's critique of the mutakallimun's excessive engagement with speculative theology and its harm to the public.

Core Idea
Theologians' debates over doubts and interpretations are harmful innovations for the masses.

After listing the essential beliefs that define a Muslim, Ghazali turns a critical eye on the mutakallimun (speculative theologians). He argues that their elaborate interpretations, questioning, and attempts to resolve doubts are bid'ah (innovation) and cause harm, especially to ordinary people. This lesson explores that critique and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic from 'وعليه فما أحدثه المتكلمون' to the end of the passage. Note the key terms: تفسير، سؤال، توجيه اشكال، حل ذلك كله، بدعة، ضرره في حق عموم.
2
Identify what the mutakallimun do
List their activities: providing interpretations (tafsir), raising questions, directing doubts, and then solving them.
3
Understand Ghazali's verdict
Ghazali calls this entire enterprise 'bid'ah' and says it harms the general public. Why might that be?
Consider that such debates may confuse laypeople or lead them away from simple faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن لم يؤمن بوجود الله سبحانه ، أو لم يؤمن بوحدانيته تعالى ، وتنزهه عن المشابهة ، والحلول والاتحاد ، أو لم يؤمن بتفرده بتدبير الكون والتصرف فيه ، واستحقاق العبادة والتقديس ، واستباح عبادة مخلوق ما من المخلوقات ، لم يؤمن بأن الله رسالات إلى خلقه ، بعث بها رسله صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم ، وأنزل عليهم كتبه عن طريق ملائكته ، أو لم يؤمن بما تضمنته الكتب من الرسل ، أو فرق بين الرسل الذين قص علينا ، فآمن بالبعض وكفر بالبعض ، أو لم يؤمن بأن الحياة الدنيا تفنى ويعقبها دار أخرى هي دار الاقامة الأبدية ، بل اعتقد أن الحياة الدنيا حياة دائمة لا الجزاء دار تنقطع ، أو اعتقد أنها تفنى فناء دائما لا بعث بعده ، ولا حساب ولا جزاء ، أو لم يؤمن بأن أصول شرع الله تعالى فيما حرم ، وفيما أوجب ، هي دينه القويم الذي يجب أن يتبع ، فحرم من تلقاء نفسه ما رأى تحريمه ، وأوجب من تلقاء نفسه ما رأى وجوبه من لم يؤمن بجانب من هذه الحقائق لا يكون مسلما ، ولا تجرى عليه أحكام المسلمين . وعليه فما أحدثه المتكلمون من تفسير وسؤال وتوجيه اشكال ، ثم اشتغالهم بحل ذلك كله ، فهو بدعة ، وضرره في حق عموم
So whoever does not believe in the existence of God Almighty, or does not believe in His oneness, His transcendence above resemblance, incarnation and union, or does not believe in His unique management of the universe and disposal therein, and His deserving worship and sanctification, and permits worship of any created being among the creations, does not believe that God has messages to His creation, sent by His messengers, peace be upon them, and sent down books to them by way of His angels, or does not believe in what the books contain from the messengers, or makes a distinction between the messengers who are narrated to us, believing in some and disbelieving in others, or does not believe that the worldly life will perish and be followed by another abode which is the abode of everlasting residence, but rather believes that the worldly life is a permanent life with no recompense, an abode that ceases, or believes that it perishes an eternal perishing with no resurrection after it, no reckoning and no recompense, or does not believe that the principles of God's law concerning what is forbidden and what is obligatory are His straight religion which must be followed, so he forbids on his own authority what he deems forbidden, and obligates on his own authority what he deems obligatory. Whoever does not believe in any aspect of these truths is not a Muslim, and the rulings of Muslims are not applied to him. Accordingly, what the mutakallimun have innovated of interpretation, question, direction of doubt, and then their occupation with solving all that, it is innovation, and its harm is upon the general public.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive statement of the essential beliefs of Islam, the negation of any of which renders one outside the fold of Islam. Ghazali lists the necessary beliefs: 1) Existence of God, 2) His oneness and transcendence above anthropomorphism, incarnation, and union, 3) His sole disposal of the universe and right to worship, 4) That God sent messages and messengers, revealed books via angels, 5) Belief in the content of the books and messengers, without distinguishing between them, 6) Belief in the afterlife: that the world will end and be followed by an eternal abode, rejecting both eternal worldliness and annihilation without resurrection, 7) That the principles of Sharia (halal and haram) are God's religion and must be followed, not based on personal opinion. Whoever fails in any of these is not Muslim. After establishing these necessary beliefs, Ghazali critiques the mutakallimun (theologians) who have innovated excessive interpretation, questioning, and the raising and solving of doubts, calling it bid'ah and harmful to the general public. This critique aligns with Ghazali's concern about the dangers of speculative theology for the masses.

Key Terms
المتكلمون
بدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All forms of theological reasoning (kalām) are always beneficial and should be pursued by everyone.
Correction: Ghazali warns that the specific methods of the mutakallimun—raising and solving doubts—are harmful innovations, especially for the masses.

Checkpoint

A) They are praiseworthy and necessary.
B) They are permissible but not recommended.
C) They are bid'ah (innovation).
D) They are obligatory for scholars.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali condemns the mutakallimun's habit of raising and solving theological doubts as an innovation that harms the faith of ordinary Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself raising theological questions or doubts in a way that confused your own faith or the faith of others? What steps can you take today to ensure your search for understanding does not become a source of harm?
?
Ghazali warns that the practices of the mutakallimun are innovations that harm the general public. Are there any religious practices or discussions you engage in that might be more about intellectual pride than sincere faith? Commit to identifying one such area and seeking guidance on it.
?
This lesson labels certain theological activities as bid'ah. Reflect on your own life: have you ever prioritized debating or solving theological puzzles over simple devotion? What change will you make to prioritize faith over speculation?

The Shahada and the Meaning of Divinity
Ghazali defines the Shahada and explains the concept of divinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two testimonies encompass all matters of tawheed and what the term 'al-uluhiyyah' (divinity) means in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
The Shahada declares Allah’s absolute self-sufficiency and our total dependence on Him.

Imam Ghazali opens by grounding the two testimonies of Islam as the foundation of all creedal matters. He then unpacks the deeper meaning of 'la ilaha illa Allah', showing that it is not merely a phrase but a declaration of Allah's independence and the creature's need. This sets the conceptual stage for understanding divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Ghazali connects the hadith of the five pillars to the encompassing nature of the Shahada.
The hadith reference is key: the Shahada is singled out in the hadith.
2
Identify the two meanings
Find where Ghazali defines the meaning of 'la ilaha illa Allah' and then the meaning of 'al-uluhiyyah'. Notice the parallel structure: negation of independence for others, affirmation for Allah.
3
Reflect on the relationship
Ask yourself: Why does Ghazali place so much emphasis on the concept of independence (istighna') and need (iftiqar)? How does this relate to the Shahada?
This links to the core idea of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخلاصة الحاصل المقصود من مجمل القول في مقدمتنا هذه التي أشرنا فيها الى ما تضمنته هذه القاعدة الجليلة: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمدا رسول الله من جهة العقيدة، أن كلمتي الشهادة هي: لا إله إلا الله، محمد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، هي أحد مباني الإسلام، إشارة إلى الحديث السابق: «بني الإسلام على خمس ... الخ». فالحديث ذكر « شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمد رسول الله »، مقتصرا على هاتين الكلمتين، لاشتمالهما على جميع مسائل التوحيد (١). وتفصيل ذلك أن معنى: لا إله إلا الله لا مستغنى عن كل ما سواه، ومفتقر إليه كل ما عداه إلا الله. ومعنى الألوهية: استغناء الاله عن كل ماسواه، وافتقار كل ما عداه إليه، فدخل تحت الاستغناء ثمانية وعشرون عقيدة: الوجود، والقدم، والبقاء، والمخالفة للحوادث، والقيام بالنفس، ووجوب السمع له، والبصر، والكلام، ولوازمها وهي: كونه سميعاً بصيراً، متكلما، وتنزهه عن الغرض في أفعاله وأحكامه
And the summary of what is intended from the totality of speech in this introduction of ours, in which we have indicated what this noble principle comprises: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' from the perspective of creed, is that the two words of testimony are: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace' are among the foundations of Islam, indicating the previous hadith: 'Islam is built upon five... etc.' So the hadith mentioned 'the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah', restricting itself to these two words, because they encompass all matters of tawheed (1). And the detail of that is that the meaning of 'there is no god but Allah' is: there is none independent of everything other than Him, and everything other than Him is in need of Him except Allah. And the meaning of divinity (al-uluhiyyah) is: the deity's independence from everything other than Him, and everything other than Him's need of Him. So under independence (al-istighna') enter twenty-eight beliefs: existence, pre-eternality, perpetuity, opposition to accidents, self-subsistence, and the necessity of hearing for Him, sight, speech, and their concomitants: that He is hearing, seeing, speaking, and His transcendence beyond purpose in His actions and judgments.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition linking the Shahada to the essential divine attributes. Imam Ghazali begins by stating that the purpose of his introduction is to clarify what is contained in the principle (al-qa'idah) of the two testimonies. The hadith of the five pillars mentions only the two testimonies because they encompass all matters of tawheed. Then he explains the meaning of 'la ilaha illa Allah': it means that there is no one independent of everything else except Allah, and all other than Him are in need of Him. This is the meaning of al-uluhiyyah (divinity): the absolute self-sufficiency of the deity and the total dependence of all creation upon Him. Under this self-sufficiency (al-istighna') fall twenty-eight creedal points; he then lists eight fundamental attributes: existence (al-wujud), pre-eternality (al-qidam), perpetuity (al-baqa'), opposition to accidents (al-mukhalafah li al-hawadith), self-subsistence (al-qiyam bi al-nafs), and the necessity of hearing (al-sam'), sight (al-basar), and speech (al-kalam), along with their concomitants (lawazim): that He is actually hearing, seeing, speaking, and that He is transcendent above any purpose in His actions and judgments. The mention of 'twenty-eight' likely presupposes further subdivision not fully carried out in this excerpt.

Key Terms
الشهادتان
لا إله إلا الله
الألوهية
الاستغناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shahada is merely a verbal formula required for entry into Islam.
Correction: Ghazali shows that the Shahada contains deep theological truths about Allah's nature and the relationship between Creator and creation.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does the hadith mention only the two testimonies among the five pillars?
A) Because they are the easiest to utter
B) Because they encompass all matters of tawheed
C) Because they are the first in order
D) Because they are the only ones mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Shahada is not just words; it expresses Allah's absolute independence and the creature's total need.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'La ilaha illa Allah', do you truly live as if you are completely dependent on Allah for every breath, every heartbeat, every moment of existence? Where in your life do you still act as if you are independent of Him?
?
If Allah's absolute self-sufficiency means He needs nothing from you, why does He still command your worship? How does that reality change the way you pray, fast, and give? Is your worship a recognition of need or an attempt to fill a void?
?
Consider a recent worry or anxiety. Did you turn to Allah with full reliance, or did you rely on your own plans, money, or people? What would it look like to truly believe that 'there is none independent except Allah' and to act on that belief today?

The Essential Divine Attributes
Ghazali lists eight essential divine attributes and their concomitants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight essential divine attributes that Imam Ghazali enumerates under the principle of divine self-sufficiency, and understand their significance.

Core Idea
God's attributes flow from His absolute self-sufficiency.

After defining divinity as self-sufficiency, Ghazali explains that under this concept fall numerous creedal points. He then lists eight key attributes that are essential to Islamic theology. This lesson focuses on understanding each of these attributes and their role in defining God's nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of attributes
Read the Arabic passage listing the attributes and their concomitants. Notice the phrase 'ثمانية وعشرون عقيدة' (twenty-eight beliefs) and the eight that follow.
The exact count of twenty-eight is not fully enumerated here; only eight are mentioned.
2
Examine each attribute
For each of the eight attributes (existence, pre-eternality, etc.), consider what they say about God's nature. How do they relate to the concept of independence?
Use a dictionary if needed for Arabic terms.
3
Understand the concomitants
Read the phrase 'ولوازمها وهي: كونه سميعاً بصيراً، متكلما' – the attributes of hearing, sight, and speech are not just potential but actual. Also note the negation of purpose in actions.
This connects to later kalam discussions.

22 Beliefs from Universal Neediness
The author enumerates 22 beliefs under neediness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the 22 beliefs that stem from the concept of universal neediness (iftiqar) and how they affirm Allah's sole agency.

Core Idea
The contingent universe's neediness yields 22 essential beliefs about Allah and His creation.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali unpacks the implications of the fact that everything other than Allah is contingent and in need of Him. He identifies 22 beliefs that follow from this foundational concept. We'll explore the list and see how each belief reinforces tawhid and the rejection of natural causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm. Then read the English translation. Notice how the author compresses a long list into a dense sentence.
The passage is brief but packed with meaning. Take your time.
2
Identify the key attributes
The passage mentions life, power, will, and knowledge as attributes of Allah. These are the divine attributes through which contingent things come into existence.
These attributes are necessary for Allah to create and sustain the universe.
3
Understand the necessary concomitants
From these attributes, we derive that Allah is living, powerful, willing, and knowing. These are His essential descriptions.
These are not separate beliefs but consequences of the attributes.
4
Recognize additional beliefs
The passage also includes oneness (tawhid), the temporal origination of the world, and the negation of natural causality. These are crucial for a correct understanding of Tawhid al-Af‘al (oneness of divine actions).
The negation of natural causality affirms that only Allah is the true agent.
5
Count the beliefs and note the opposites
The total is twenty-two, counting also the opposites of each belief. This shows how comprehensive the concept of neediness is.
The exact enumeration is a mnemonic for the student.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل تحت الإفتقار : اثنان وعشرون عقيدة : الممكنات يؤثر بقوة الحياة وعموم القدرة ، والارادة ، والعلم ، ولوازمها ، وهي : كونه : حيا ، وقادرا ، ومريدا ، وعالما، والوحدانية ، وحدوث العالم بأسره ، وأن لا تأثير لشيء من الكائنات في أثر ما بالطبع ، وأضدادها ، فجملتها اثنان وعشرون عقيدة
And under neediness (iftiqar) there enter twenty-two beliefs: that contingent things are effected by the power of life and the generality of power, will, and knowledge, and their necessary concomitants, which are: His being living, powerful, willing, knowing, and oneness, and the temporal origination of the entire world, and that nothing from among existing things has any effect by nature in any effect, and their opposites. So their total is twenty-two beliefs.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage enumerates the 22 beliefs that fall under the concept of universal neediness (iftiqar). The author lists the attributes of Allah that are related to His interaction with creation: life, power, will, knowledge, and their necessary implications (He is living, powerful, willing, knowing). Then he includes oneness (wahdaniyya), the temporal origination of the world (huduth al-alam), and the negation of natural causality (that no created thing has any effect by nature). These beliefs all follow from the fact that everything other than Allah is contingent and in need of Him. The opposites are also included.

Key Terms
الإفتقار
الممكنات
الحياة
القدرة
الإرادة
العلم
الوحدانية
حدوث العالم
نفي التأثير بالطبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that created things have inherent causal power (e.g., fire burns by its nature).
Correction: The passage states that nothing has effect by nature; all effects are directly from Allah. This guards against the error of attributing independent agency to creation.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The lesson says contingent things are effected by Allah's power, will, and knowledge. Do you live as if your daily affairs are under His control? Where do you still feel independent?
?
The 22 beliefs include that Allah is living, powerful, willing, knowing. Which of these attributes do you neglect in your daily awareness? How would your actions change if you truly felt His power and knowledge?

All Creation is Originated by Allah's Action with Perfect Wisdom and Justice
Ghazali affirms that all creation is by Allah's action, done with wisdom and justice, and explains why injustice is impossible for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every existent besides Allah is originated by His action, done with perfect wisdom and justice, and why divine justice cannot be compared to human justice.

Core Idea
Allah alone originates all existence, and His justice is beyond human measure.

Imam al-Ghazali opens his discussion of divine actions by making a sweeping claim: nothing exists besides Allah except that it is brought into being by His act. He immediately connects this to His attributes of wisdom and justice, explaining that His justice is incomparable because He owns everything. This passage establishes the fundamental framework for understanding Allah's relationship with creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening declaration
Read the first statement carefully: 'لا موجود سواه إلا وهو حادث بفعله'. Notice the absolute scope.
This is the central claim of the lesson.
2
Examine the list of creatures
Ghazali enumerates every category of being. Notice the comprehensive range from angels to inanimate objects.
The list emphasizes that nothing is created by anyone else.
3
Reflect on divine justice
Read the explanation of why Allah's justice is incomparable. Focus on the phrase 'لا يصادف لغيره ملكا'.
Injustice is impossible for Allah because He owns everything.
4
Study the footnote on creative terms
Read the footnote distinguishing ikhtira', ijad, khalq, ibda', and fi'l. Note that 'action' is real for Allah, metaphorical for creatures.
5
Connect justice to action
Understand that true knowledge of Allah's justice comes from contemplating His actions in the cosmos.
This is from the latter part of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الافعال : وأنه سبحانه وتعالى لا موجود سواه الا وهو حادث بفعله (۱) ، وفائض من عدله على أحسن الوجوه وأكملها ، وأتمها وأعدلها ، وأنه حكيم في أفعاله(۲) ، عادل في أقضيته (۳) ، لا يقاس عدله بعدل العباد (٤) ، إذ العبد يتصور منه الظلم بتصرفه في ملك غيره ، ولا يتصور الظلم من الله تعالى ، فإنه لا يصادف لغيره ملكا حتى يكون تصرفه فيه ظلما ، فكل ما سواه من إنس وجن ، وملك وشيطان ، وسماء وأرض وحيوان ، ونبات وجماد، وجوهر وعرض ، ومدرك ومحسوس ـ حادث اخترعه بقدرته بعد العدم اختراعا ، وأنشأه إنشاء بعد أن لم يكن شيئا ، إذ كان في الازل موجودا وحده ولم يكن معه غيره (۹) ، فأحدث الخلق بعد ذلك إظهارا لقدرته (٦) ، وتحقيقا لما سبق من إرادته ، ولما حق في الأزل من كلمته (۷) . (۱) الفرق بين الإختراع والإيجاد والخلق والإبداع أن الاختراع خاص بالله تعالى، وكذا الإيجاد والإبداع والخلق ؛ وأما الفعل فإنه يطلق على القديم والحادث إلا أنه في حقه تعالى حقيقة ، لأنه هو الذي اخترعه ، وأما في حق الحادث فمجاز، وإنما هو عبارة عن مباشرتهم للأشياء وتحريكهم لها (۲) بإصابة مراده على حسب قصده (۳) على الحقيقة لا يوصف بالجور والظلم (٤) العادل هو الذي يصدر منه فعل العدل المضاد للجور والظلم ، ولن يعرف العادل من لم يعرف عدله ، ولا يعرف عدله من لم يعرف فعله ، فمن أراد أن يفهم هذا الوصف فينبغي أن يحيط علما بأفعال الله تعالى من ملكوت السموات ، إلى منتهى الثرى ، حتى إذا بهره جمال الحضرة الربوبية وحيره اعتدالها وانتظامها تعلق بفهمه شيء من معاني عدل الله في خلقه (٥) يشاركه أو يماثله في ذاته وصفاته وأفعاله ، وفي هذا إشارة الى أن احداثه تعالى ذلك كان باختياره وحده ولا هو استكمال كمال زائد على ما كان قبل إحداثه (٦) وفي نسخة أخرى : فأحدث الخلق بعد عدمه إظهاراً لقدرته (۷) كلمته التي لا تبدل ، وفيه إشارة الى أن تأثير القدرة فرع تأثير الإرادة، إذ لا يوجد تعالى شيئاً من الممكنات ، أو يعدم بقدرته إلا ما أراده تعالى وجوده أو اعدامه، وتأثير الإرادة على وفق العلم ، فكل ما علم تعالى أنه يكون من الممكنات أو لا يكون فذلك مراده
Actions: And that He, exalted and glorified, - there is no existent besides Him except that it is originated by His action (1), and overflowing from His justice in the best and most complete ways, the most perfect and most just. And that He is Wise in His actions (2), Just in His decrees (3). His justice is not measured by the justice of servants (4), for the servant can be conceived of injustice by his disposal of another's property, but injustice cannot be conceived from Allah Almighty, for He does not encounter another's property so that His disposal of it would be injustice. So everything besides Him—humans, jinn, angels, devils, heavens, earth, animals, plants, inanimate objects, substance, accident, perceived and sensed—is an originated thing He invented by His power after non-existence, as an invention, and He brought it into being after it was nothing, for He alone existed in pre-eternity and there was nothing with Him (5). Then He brought forth creation after that as a manifestation of His power (6), and a fulfillment of what preceded from His will, and of what was decreed in pre-eternity from His word (7). (1) The difference between invention (ikhtirāʿ), bringing into existence (ījād), creation (khalq), and origination (ibdāʿ) is that invention is specific to Allah Almighty, likewise bringing into existence, origination, and creation. As for action (fiʿl), it is applied to the eternal and the originated, except that in His case it is real (ḥaqīqa) because He is the one who invented it, while in the case of the originated it is metaphorical (majāz), and it is merely an expression of their direct involvement with things and their movement of them. (2) By hitting His purpose according to His intent. (3) In reality, He is not described with injustice and wrongdoing. (4) The just (al-ʿādil) is one from whom the act of justice opposite to injustice and wrongdoing issues. The just cannot be known by one who does not know His justice, and His justice cannot be known by one who does not know His action. So whoever wants to understand this attribute should encompass knowledge of the actions of Allah Almighty from the dominion of the heavens to the depths of the earth, until when the beauty of the divine presence dazzles him and its balance and organization bewilders him, something of the meanings of Allah's justice in His creation attaches to his understanding. (5) To share or resemble Him in His essence, attributes, and actions. In this is an indication that His bringing about of that was by His will alone, and it is not a completion of a perfection additional to what was before He brought it about. (6) In another copy: Then He brought forth creation after its non-existence as a manifestation of His power. (7) His word that does not change. In this is an indication that the effect of power is a branch of the effect of will, for Allah does not bring any possible thing into existence or non-existence by His power except what He wills to exist or non-exist. And the effect of will is in accordance with knowledge, so whatever Allah knows of possible things that will be or will not be, that is His will.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on divine actions (al-afʿāl). The author, Imam al-Ghazali, begins by stating that no existent besides Allah exists except that it is originated by His action (ḥādith bi-fiʿlihi). Everything proceeds from His justice in the best, most complete, perfect, and just manner. He is Wise (ḥakīm) in His actions, hitting His purpose, and Just (ʿādil) in His decrees, not described with injustice. His justice is incomparable to human justice: human injustice arises from disposing of another's property, but Allah owns everything, so no injustice is conceivable. All beings—humans, jinn, angels, devils, heavens, earth, animals, plants, inanimate objects, substances, accidents—are originated by His power from non-existence. He alone existed in pre-eternity (al-azal) with nothing else. He created them to manifest His power, fulfill His will, and realize His eternal word. The footnotes elaborate: [1] distinguishes inventive terms (ikhtirāʿ, ījād, khalq, ibdāʿ) as exclusive to Allah. The term 'action' (fiʿl) is real (ḥaqīqa) for Allah, metaphorical for creatures who merely directly engage with things. [2] His wisdom means hitting His purpose. [3] Justice means no injustice. [4] True understanding of divine justice requires contemplating His actions in the cosmos. [5] Nothing shares or resembles His essence, attributes, and actions; creation does not add perfection to Him. [6] Alternate wording. [7] His word is unchangeable; divine power operates under will, will under knowledge; whatever Allah knows will be or not be is what He wills.

حادث
اختراع
إيجاد

عادل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's justice is like human justice and can be measured by human standards.
Correction: The passage states that Allah's justice is not measured by the justice of servants (لا يقاس عدله بعدل العباد) because He does not encounter another's property; injustice is inconceivable for Him.

Checkpoint
Why can injustice not be attributed to Allah according to the passage?
A) Because He is merciful
B) Because He does not own anything
C) Because He does not encounter another's property
D) Because He is all-powerful

Key Takeaway
Everything besides Allah is created by His action with perfect justice that is beyond human comparison.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation that feels deeply unfair, do you truly believe that Allah's action in it is just, even if you cannot see the wisdom? What would it cost you to surrender that complaint to Him today?
?
If everything besides Allah is created by His act, does your daily life reflect that conviction? In what area are you still acting as if your own efforts are the ultimate source of your success or failure?
?
Allah's justice is not like human justice—He owes nothing to anyone. Does this truth make you feel more awe or more distance from Him? How can you cultivate a heart that worships Him not for what you expect to receive, but for who He is?

Allah's Existence
intermediate

The Purpose of Creation and the Hierarchy of Divine Attributes
Ghazali explains the purpose of creation and the hierarchical relationship between divine power, will, and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose of creation as a manifestation of Allah's power, will, and word, and the hierarchical relationship between His power, will, and knowledge.

Core Idea
Creation manifests Allah's power, fulfills His will, and realizes His eternal word.

Having established that all creation is by Allah's action, Ghazali now explains why Allah brought creation into existence. He states that it is to manifest His power, fulfill His will, and realize His eternal word. The footnotes further elaborate on the relationship between these divine attributes, showing that power operates under will, and will under knowledge. This lesson presents that final part of the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the purpose statements
Read the sentence: 'فأحدث الخلق بعد ذلك إظهارا لقدرته، وتحقيقا لما سبق من إرادته، ولما حق في الأزل من كلمته'.
Three purposes are mentioned: manifestation of power, fulfillment of will, realization of word.
2
Note that creation adds no perfection
Study the footnote: 'أن احداثه تعالى ذلك كان باختياره وحده ولا هو استكمال كمال زائد'.
Creation is purely by His choice and does not increase His perfection.
3
Examine the hierarchy of attributes
Read the footnote about power being a branch of will, and will being according to knowledge.
This shows the logical order: Knowledge → Will → Power → Creation.
4
Understand the scope of will
Notice that Allah only creates or annihilates what He wills, and His will matches His knowledge of what will be.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الافعال : وأنه سبحانه وتعالى لا موجود سواه الا وهو حادث بفعله (۱) ، وفائض من عدله على أحسن الوجوه وأكملها ، وأتمها وأعدلها ، وأنه حكيم في أفعاله(۲) ، عادل في أقضيته (۳) ، لا يقاس عدله بعدل العباد (٤) ، إذ العبد يتصور منه الظلم بتصرفه في ملك غيره ، ولا يتصور الظلم من الله تعالى ، فإنه لا يصادف لغيره ملكا حتى يكون تصرفه فيه ظلما ، فكل ما سواه من إنس وجن ، وملك وشيطان ، وسماء وأرض وحيوان ، ونبات وجماد، وجوهر وعرض ، ومدرك ومحسوس ـ حادث اخترعه بقدرته بعد العدم اختراعا ، وأنشأه إنشاء بعد أن لم يكن شيئا ، إذ كان في الازل موجودا وحده ولم يكن معه غيره (۹) ، فأحدث الخلق بعد ذلك إظهارا لقدرته (٦) ، وتحقيقا لما سبق من إرادته ، ولما حق في الأزل من كلمته (۷) . (۱) الفرق بين الإختراع والإيجاد والخلق والإبداع أن الاختراع خاص بالله تعالى، وكذا الإيجاد والإبداع والخلق ؛ وأما الفعل فإنه يطلق على القديم والحادث إلا أنه في حقه تعالى حقيقة ، لأنه هو الذي اخترعه ، وأما في حق الحادث فمجاز، وإنما هو عبارة عن مباشرتهم للأشياء وتحريكهم لها (۲) بإصابة مراده على حسب قصده (۳) على الحقيقة لا يوصف بالجور والظلم (٤) العادل هو الذي يصدر منه فعل العدل المضاد للجور والظلم ، ولن يعرف العادل من لم يعرف عدله ، ولا يعرف عدله من لم يعرف فعله ، فمن أراد أن يفهم هذا الوصف فينبغي أن يحيط علما بأفعال الله تعالى من ملكوت السموات ، إلى منتهى الثرى ، حتى إذا بهره جمال الحضرة الربوبية وحيره اعتدالها وانتظامها تعلق بفهمه شيء من معاني عدل الله في خلقه (٥) يشاركه أو يماثله في ذاته وصفاته وأفعاله ، وفي هذا إشارة الى أن احداثه تعالى ذلك كان باختياره وحده ولا هو استكمال كمال زائد على ما كان قبل إحداثه (٦) وفي نسخة أخرى : فأحدث الخلق بعد عدمه إظهاراً لقدرته (۷) كلمته التي لا تبدل ، وفيه إشارة الى أن تأثير القدرة فرع تأثير الإرادة، إذ لا يوجد تعالى شيئاً من الممكنات ، أو يعدم بقدرته إلا ما أراده تعالى وجوده أو اعدامه، وتأثير الإرادة على وفق العلم ، فكل ما علم تعالى أنه يكون من الممكنات أو لا يكون فذلك مراده
Actions: And that He, exalted and glorified, - there is no existent besides Him except that it is originated by His action (1), and overflowing from His justice in the best and most complete ways, the most perfect and most just. And that He is Wise in His actions (2), Just in His decrees (3). According to the passage, what are the three purposes of creation?
A) Manifestation of power, fulfillment of will, realization of word

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If creation exists solely to manifest Allah's power, will, and word, what does that reveal about the ultimate purpose of your own life? Are you living to display His attributes or to serve your own?
?

?
When life's events confuse or trouble you, do you truly trust that they align with Allah's perfect knowledge and will? What would change in your heart if you fully embraced this harmony of divine attributes?
