The First Maqam: The Star Argument
Ibrahim's first argumentative station using the setting of celestial bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Prophet Ibrahim's observation of celestial bodies serves as a rational proof for the existence of God, as used by theologians.

Core Idea
The setting of stars proves they are created, pointing to a Creator.

Imam al-Ghazali begins by praising Ibrahim's argumentation and then presents the first of his four argumentative stations. This initial argument, based on the setting of celestial bodies, is identified as the very method used by theologians (mutakallimun). It is a foundational rational proof that temporality implies a creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the phrase 'طريق المتكلمين' – the way of the theologians.
2
Identify the logical steps
The passage outlines three steps: observing the star's setting (afool), deducing its temporality (huduth), and then deducing the need for a creator (muhdith).
This is a classic kalam argument known as the argument from temporality.
3
Reflect on the method
Ask yourself why this method is praised and why it's called the method of the theologians.
It shows that reason and revelation work together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ ذكر سبحانه احتجاج إبراهيم ومجادلته وإفحامه خصمه في معرض الثناء عليه والمدح له، وهنا ناسب أن نذكر أن لسيدنا إبراهيم عليه السلام في الاحتجاج مقامات: أحدها: الآية نفسها وهو قوله تعالى: (فلما جن عليه الليل رأى كوكباً قال هذا ربي) .. الخ وهذا طريق المتكلمين، فإنه استدل بأفولها وتغيرها على حدوثها، ثم استدل بحدوثها على وجود محدثها. وثانيها: حاله مع أبيه وهو قوله: (يا أبت لم تعبد ما لا يسمع ولا يبصر ولا يغني عنك شيئاً) الخ الآيات. وثالثها: حاله مع قومه تارة بالقول وتارة بالفعل، أما القول فهو قوله: (ما هذه التماثيل التي أنتم لها عاكفون) وأما الفعل فقوله: (فجعلهم جذاذاً إلا كبيراً لهم). ورابعها: حاله مع ملك زمانه وهو الذي ذكره المصنف، ثم إنه عليه السلام لما استدل بحدوثها على وجود محدثها كما أخبر الله تعالى عنه في قوله: (يا قوم إني بريء مما تشركون، إني وجهت وجهي للذي قطر السموات والأرض) عظم شأنه بذلك.
When He, glorified, mentioned Ibrahim's argumentation and his disputation and his silencing of his opponent in context of praise and commendation for him, it is appropriate here to mention that our master Ibrahim (peace be upon him) has stations in argumentation: First: the verse itself, which is His saying: 'When the night covered him, he saw a star; he said: This is my Lord' etc. And this is the method of the theologians, for he deduced from its setting and change its temporality, then deduced from its temporality the existence of its Originator. Second: his situation with his father, which is his saying: 'O my father, why do you worship that which neither hears nor sees nor benefits you in any way' etc. the verses. Third: his situation with his people sometimes by word and sometimes by deed. As for the word, it is his saying: 'What are these images to which you are devoted?' And as for the deed, it is his saying: 'So he made them fragments, except a large one of them.' Fourth: his situation with the king of his time, which is what the author mentioned. Then when he (peace be upon him) deduced from their temporality the existence of their Originator, as Allah informed about him in His saying: 'O my people, indeed I am free from what you associate. Indeed, I have turned my face toward He who created the heavens and the earth,' his status was magnified by that.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage enumerates the four argumentative stations (maqamat) of Prophet Ibrahim (AS). The author begins by noting that Allah mentions Ibrahim's disputation as praise. Then he lists: (1) The argument from the setting of celestial bodies, which is the method of the theologians (mutakallimun): Ibrahim observed the star, moon, and sun setting, deducing their temporality, and from temporality he inferred a Creator. (2) His verbal argument with his father, who worshiped idols that cannot perceive or help. (3) His argument with his people, both verbally (rebuking their idolatry) and practically (breaking the idols while leaving the largest). (4) His argument with the king (Namrud), as mentioned by the author (al-Musannif), where Ibrahim used the same temporal argument to prove the Creator, citing the Quranic verse about turning his face to the Originator of the heavens and earth. Each station illustrates a distinct method of prophetic argumentation.

Key Terms
أفول
حدوث
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Ibrahim deduce from the setting of the star?
A) That the star was his Lord
B) That the star is temporal and requires a creator
C) That the star is eternal
D) That stars are gods

Key Takeaway
Ibrahim's first argument uses the observed temporality of celestial bodies to prove the existence of a Creator, a method foundational to Islamic theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you gaze at the stars tonight, will you let their setting remind you of the Creator, or will you remain heedless? Commit to one moment each day to reflect on a changing thing and say 'I do not love those that set.'
?
Ibrahim's argument begins with a simple observation: things change. What in your life have you been clinging to that is guaranteed to change and fade? Are you ready to place your trust solely in the Eternal?
?
The passage shows that this is the method of the theologians—a logical proof you can use yourself. Will you take the time to learn and internalize it so it becomes a source of certainty in your heart? Set a specific plan to study one more proof of Allah's existence.

The Second Maqam: Argument with His Father
Ibrahim's argument with his father against idol worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Prophet Ibrahim argued against idol worship by emphasizing the idols' inability to perceive or benefit.

Core Idea
Idols are powerless to hear, see, or help – why worship them?

The second station of Ibrahim's argumentation is his dialogue with his father, who was an idol worshiper. Ibrahim's approach here is to point out the helplessness of the idols through a simple, logical question that any rational person can appreciate.

Guided Path
1
Read the excerpt about Ibrahim and his father
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the verse quoted: 'O my father, why do you worship that which neither hears nor sees nor benefits you in any way?'
Notice the tone is gentle yet logical.
2
Analyze the argument
Ibrahim uses three negatives: the idols cannot hear, cannot see, and cannot benefit. This covers all possible reasons for worship – they are completely powerless.
This is a rhetorical question that forces reflection.
3
Connect to the broader lesson
Understand that this maqam shows Ibrahim's use of direct rational engagement with his own family.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ ذكر سبحانه احتجاج إبراهيم ومجادلته وإفحامه خصمه في معرض الثناء عليه والمدح له، وهنا ناسب أن نذكر أن لسيدنا إبراهيم عليه السلام في الاحتجاج مقامات: أحدها: الآية نفسها وهو قوله تعالى: (فلما جن عليه الليل رأى كوكباً قال هذا ربي) .. الخ وهذا طريق المتكلمين، فإنه استدل بأفولها وتغيرها على حدوثها، ثم استدل بحدوثها على وجود محدثها. وثانيها: حاله مع أبيه وهو قوله: (يا أبت لم تعبد ما لا يسمع ولا يبصر ولا يغني عنك شيئاً) الخ الآيات. وثالثها: حاله مع قومه تارة بالقول وتارة بالفعل، أما القول فهو قوله: (ما هذه التماثيل التي أنتم لها عاكفون) وأما الفعل فقوله: (فجعلهم جذاذاً إلا كبيراً لهم). ورابعها: حاله مع ملك زمانه وهو الذي ذكره المصنف، ثم إنه عليه السلام لما استدل بحدوثها على وجود محدثها كما أخبر الله تعالى عنه في قوله: (يا قوم إني بريء مما تشركون، إني وجهت وجهي للذي قطر السموات والأرض) عظم شأنه بذلك.
When He, glorified, mentioned Ibrahim's argumentation and his disputation and his silencing of his opponent in context of praise and commendation for him, it is appropriate here to mention that our master Ibrahim (peace be upon him) has stations in argumentation: First: the verse itself, which is His saying: 'When the night covered him, he saw a star; he said: This is my Lord' etc. And this is the method of the theologians, for he deduced from its setting and change its temporality, then deduced from its temporality the existence of its Originator. Second: his situation with his father, which is his saying: 'O my father, why do you worship that which neither hears nor sees nor benefits you in any way' etc. the verses. Third: his situation with his people sometimes by word and sometimes by deed. As for the word, it is his saying: 'What are these images to which you are devoted?' And as for the deed, it is his saying: 'So he made them fragments, except a large one of them.' Fourth: his situation with the king of his time, which is what the author mentioned. Then when he (peace be upon him) deduced from their temporality the existence of their Originator, as Allah informed about him in His saying: 'O my people, indeed I am free from what you associate. Indeed, I have turned my face toward He who created the heavens and the earth,' his status was magnified by that.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage enumerates the four argumentative stations (maqamat) of Prophet Ibrahim (AS). The author begins by noting that Allah mentions Ibrahim's disputation as praise. Then he lists: (1) The argument from the setting of celestial bodies, which is the method of the theologians (mutakallimun): Ibrahim observed the star, moon, and sun setting, deducing their temporality, and from temporality he inferred a Creator. (2) His verbal argument with his father, who worshiped idols that cannot perceive or help. (3) His argument with his people, both verbally (rebuking their idolatry) and practically (breaking the idols while leaving the largest). (4) His argument with the king (Namrud), as mentioned by the author (al-Musannif), where Ibrahim used the same temporal argument to prove the Creator, citing the Quranic verse about turning his face to the Originator of the heavens and earth. Each station illustrates a distinct method of prophetic argumentation.

Key Takeaway
Ibrahim's argument with his father highlights the futility of worshipping beings devoid of sensory perception and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Third Maqam: Argument with His People
Ibrahim's argument with his people through words and deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibrahim combined verbal reasoning and physical action to demonstrate the falsehood of idol worship.

Core Idea
Ibrahim used both words and deeds to break the idols' spell.

The third station shows Ibrahim engaging his people through two methods: first by verbal rebuke questioning their devotion to statues, and then by physically breaking the idols, leaving only the largest one intact. This dual approach reinforced his message powerfully.

Guided Path
1
Read about the two parts of the argument
Read the Arabic and translation that separately describe Ibrahim's words and his actions.
Notice the structure: 'أما القول... وأما الفعل'.
2
Analyze the verbal argument
Ibrahim asks: 'What are these images to which you are devoted?' – this challenges their blind devotion.
3
Analyze the action
He breaks the idols except the largest one, which sets up a later lesson about its inability to do anything.
This act is dramatic and draws attention.

The Fourth Maqam: Argument with the King
Ibrahim's argument with the king and the summary of his exaltation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibrahim argued with the king of his time, using the same temporal argument to prove the existence of the Creator.

Core Idea
Ibrahim's argumentation method is consistent across all four stations.

The final station involves Ibrahim's confrontation with a powerful king (often identified as Nimrod). Here, Ibrahim uses the same reasoning as in the first station: from the temporality of created things, he deduces the existence of their Creator. This consistency shows that the essence of faith is based on rational proof.

Read the passage about the king

Ibrahim again uses the argument from temporality (حدوث) to conclude the existence of the Creator (محدث).
This shows the universality of this proof.
3
Reflect on the outcome
The passage ends by noting that Ibrahim's status was magnified by this argument.

Prophetic Debates Focus on Tawhid and Prophethood
Cites Quranic verses to show prophets debated only tawhid and nubuwwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophetic debates centered exclusively on tawhid (oneness of Allah) and prophethood, as evidenced by the Quran.

Core Idea
Prophetic debates were not about legal details but about the core of faith: tawhid and prophethood.

The Quran records numerous debates between prophets and their people. Imam al-Ghazali points out a pattern: these arguments consistently revolve around two fundamental principles. This lesson examines the Quranic evidence he cites and the methodological insight it provides for prioritizing theological topics.

Guided Path
1
Examine the first two verses
Read the verses about Ibrahim and Nuh. Notice how each involves a disputation. What is being argued about?
The verses don't specify the topic explicitly; the author uses them as evidence of disputation.
2
Consider the third verse and its context
Read the verse about Musa and Pharaoh. The phrase 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' is the question. This is about tawhid.
The author cuts off at 'a clear sign' but the core is clear.
3
Understand the broader conclusion
The author states that the entire Quran is a muhajja (disputation) with disbelievers, and it is known that these debates were not about legal rulings, so they must be about tawhid and nubuwwa.
This establishes a priority in da'wah and theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال عز وجل: (وتلك حجتنا آتيناها إبراهيم على قومه) وقال تعالى: (قالوا يا نوح قد جادلتنا فأكثرت جدالنا) وقال تعالى في قصة فرعون: (وما رب العالمين) إلى قوله: (أولو جئتك بشيء مبين) وعلى الجملة فالقرآن من أوله إلى آخره محاجة مع الكفار. والمراد: أنه معلوم أن مجادلة الرسول مع الكفار لا تكون في تفاصيل الأحكام الشرعية، فلم يبق إلا أنها كانت في التوحيد والنبوة.
And He, exalted, said: 'And that is Our argument which We gave to Abraham against his people.' And He said: 'They said, O Noah, you have argued with us and increased our argument.' And He said in the story of Pharaoh: 'And what is the Lord of the worlds?' up to His saying: 'Or have I come to you with a clear sign?' And in summary, the Quran from its beginning to its end is a disputation with the disbelievers. And the intent: it is known that the disputation of the Messenger with the disbelievers is not in the details of legal rulings; so nothing remains except that it was concerning tawhid and prophethood.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents Quranic evidence that prophetic arguments centered on core beliefs. The author cites three verses: (1) Allah giving Ibrahim a conclusive argument against his people; (2) Noah's people acknowledging his frequent disputation; (3) Pharaoh's question to Musa about the Lord of the worlds, leading to Musa's challenge with a clear sign. The author then draws a general conclusion: the entire Quran is a disputation (muhajja) with disbelievers. He clarifies that these debates were not about subsidiary legal rulings (tafasil al-ahkam al-shar'iyya) but solely about tawhid (oneness of God) and nubuwwa (prophethood). This establishes the theological priority of these two principles.

Key Terms
حجة
مجادلة
محاجة
توحيد
نبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might assume prophets debated all aspects of religion, including legal rulings.
Correction: The author specifies they focused only on tawhid and prophethood, not on details of legal rulings.

Checkpoint

A) Detailed legal rulings
B) Tawhid and prophethood
C) Social and political issues
D) Stories of previous nations

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you talk to someone about Islam, do you naturally start with tawhid and the prophethood of Muhammad, or do you find yourself arguing about secondary issues like food, dress, or politics? What does this lesson reveal about your approach?
?
Knowing that the entire Quran is a disputation with disbelievers, how does this change the way you read or recite it? Are you reading it as a personal challenge to your own faith, or as a book of rules?
?
The prophets focused their debates on the core message. What does this say about your own priorities in inviting others to Islam? Are you willing to set aside less important issues to establish the foundations? If not, what holds you back?

Musa's Proofs Mirror Ibrahim's in Content and Order
Musa’s proofs mirror Ibrahim’s in content and order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophet Musa (peace be upon him) used the same three proofs as Ibrahim (peace be upon him) to establish tawhid, and how he then built proofs of prophethood upon that foundation.

Core Idea
Musa’s arguments with Pharaoh exactly followed Ibrahim’s three tawhid proofs.

This passage reveals a remarkable consistency in the prophetic message: Musa employed the same logical sequence of arguments that Ibrahim had used centuries earlier. By examining the parallel verses, we see how tawhid is established through creation and guidance, life and death, and dominion over the cosmos. Only after this foundation is laid does the proof of prophethood follow, showing the proper order of theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author’s claim that Musa did not add anything beyond Ibrahim’s proofs.
The author is using Qur’anic citations from Surah Taha and Surah al-Shu‘ara.
2
Identify the three matching proofs
Look at each of the three proofs the author compares: (1) creation and guidance, (2) life and death, (3) dominion over the sun. Note the specific verses quoted for Ibrahim and Musa.
The proofs are presented in the same order for both prophets.
3
Understand the logical sequence
Notice that after the three tawhid proofs, Musa presents a proof of prophethood ('a clear sign'). The author says this shows that prophethood is based on tawhid.
This order teaches us about priority: knowledge of Allah comes before acceptance of messengers.
4
Reflect on the method
Ask yourself: Why do you think the Qur’an shows this consistency? What does it tell us about the unity of the prophetic message?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولتوضيح المراد نذكر أن سيدنا موسى عليه وعلى نبينا أفضل الصلاة والسلام، ما كان يقول في الاستدلال بزيادة على دلائل إبراهيم عليه السلام؛ وذلك لأنه حكى الله تعالى عنه في سورة طه، أن فرعون قال له ولهارون: فمن ربكما يا موسى قال: ربنا الذي أعطى كل شيء خلقه ثم هدى؛ وهذا هو الدليل الذي ذكره إبراهيم عليه السلام حيث قال: (الذي خلقني فهو يهديني). ثم حكى الله تعالى عن موسى في الشعراء، أنه قال لفرعون: (ربكم ورب آبائكم الأولين)، وهذا هو الدليل الذي عول عليه إبراهيم عليه السلام في قوله: (ربي الذي يحيي ويميت). فلما لم يكتف فرعون بذلك وطالبه بدليل آخر قال موسى: (رب المشرق والمغرب)، وهذا هو الذي عول عليه إبراهيم عليه السلام في قوله: (فإن الله يأتي بالشمس من المشرق فأت بها من المغرب). ثم إن موسى عليه السلام، لما فرغ من تقدير دلائل التوحيد ذكر بعده دلائل النبوة فقال: (أولو جئتك بشيء مبين). وهذا يدل على أنه عليه السلام فرع بيان النبوة على بيان التوحيد والمعرفة.
And to clarify the intent, we mention that our master Musa (peace be upon him and upon our Prophet the best of prayers and peace) did not say in argumentation anything additional to the proofs of Ibrahim (peace be upon him). That is because Allah reported from him in Surah Taha that Pharaoh said to him and Harun: 'Who is your Lord, O Musa?' He said: 'Our Lord is He who gave each thing its form then guided [it].' This is the proof that Ibrahim mentioned when he said: 'He who created me and guides me.' Then Allah reported from Musa in al-Shu'ara that he said to Pharaoh: 'Your Lord and the Lord of your forefathers.' This is the proof that Ibrahim relied upon in his saying: 'My Lord is He who gives life and causes death.' When Pharaoh was not satisfied with that and demanded another proof, Musa said: 'Lord of the east and the west.' This is what Ibrahim relied upon in his saying: 'Indeed Allah brings the sun from the east, so bring it from the west.' Then when Musa finished presenting the proofs of tawhid, he mentioned after that the proofs of prophethood and said: 'Or I will bring you a clear sign.' This indicates that he made the clarification of prophethood dependent upon the clarification of tawhid and knowledge.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage demonstrates that Musa's arguments with Pharaoh were identical in content and sequence to Ibrahim's proofs. The author compares three matching proofs: (1) Creation and guidance: Ibrahim says 'He who created me and guides me'; Musa says 'Our Lord is He who gave each thing its form then guided it.' (2) Life and death: Ibrahim says 'My Lord is He who gives life and causes death'; Musa says 'Your Lord and the Lord of your forefathers.' (3) Dominion over the sun: Ibrahim challenges with bringing the sun from the west; Musa says 'Lord of the east and the west.' After establishing tawhid with these three proofs, Musa then presented proofs of prophethood ('a clear sign'), showing that prophethood is built upon the foundation of tawhid and knowledge.

Key Terms
دلائل
توحيد
نبوة
استدلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Musa brought novel arguments to Pharaoh, independent of earlier prophets.
Correction: The passage shows that Musa’s arguments were exactly the same as Ibrahim’s in both content and order, demonstrating the unity of the prophetic message.

Checkpoint
What does Musa's presentation of proofs of prophethood after proofs of tawhid indicate?
A) Prophethood is independent of tawhid
B) Tawhid is the foundation for prophethood
C) Prophethood is more important than tawhid
D) Musa disagreed with Ibrahim's order

Key Takeaway
Musa’s arguments for tawhid were not novel; they mirrored Ibrahim’s in both content and order, and he presented prophethood only after establishing tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that tawhid is the foundation of everything in your life, or do you sometimes treat it as a theoretical concept while living as if other things come first? What would change if you genuinely made tawhid the basis for your actions today?
?
Musa presented prophethood only after establishing tawhid. In your own life, have you built your understanding of prophethood and following the Prophet on a solid foundation of knowing Allah? Or have you rushed to practices without establishing your heart's certainty in Allah? What step can you take today to strengthen your tawhid first?
?
The prophets did not innovate in their message; they all called to the same truth. Does your life reflect the unity of the prophetic message, or do you pick and choose, elevating some teachings over others? How can you align yourself more fully with the consistent call of all the prophets?

The Quran's Arguments on Three Core Doctrines
Ghazali notes Quran's content as arguments on tawhid, Maker, resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran's primary content is argumentation (ḥujaj, adilla, barāhīn) focused on three fundamental topics: tawhid, proofs for the Creator, and the resurrection.

Core Idea
The Quran is a book of theological arguments, not just stories.

This passage from Ghazali's commentary reinforces a key point: the Quran is not merely a collection of laws and narratives; it is filled with reasoned arguments and proofs. Specifically, it centers on three essential doctrinal areas that form the backbone of Islamic belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

These cover core creedal areas.
3
Note the alternative wording
The passage begins with 'Wa fī nuskhah ukhrā: mujāhalat al-kuffār.' Reflect on why the Quran's arguments are framed as disputation with disbelievers.
This highlights the Quran’s polemical context.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider how this shapes our understanding of the Quran’s purpose. Why is it important that the Quran is filled with proofs rather than just commands?
This connects to the broader theme of rational theology.

And in another copy: 'disputation of the disbelievers.' And the intent is that it is filled with arguments, proofs, and evidences in matters of tawhid, establishing the Maker, and the resurrection.

Commentary

It specifies three core topics: (1) matters of tawhid (divine oneness), (2) establishing the Maker (ithbāt al-ṣāni'), and (3) the resurrection (al-ma'ād). The alternative reading 'mujāhalat al-kuffār' (disputation of the disbelievers) underscores that the Quran's argumentative nature is directed against disbelief. This passage confirms that the Quran's primary concern is theological reasoning, not merely legal or narrative content.

The Three Cardinal Quranic Proofs for Tawhid, Nubuwwa, and Ba'th
Ghazali enumerates three key Quranic proofs for tawhid, nubuwwa, and ba'th and asserts the Qur'an's supremacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational Quranic verses that mutakallimūn rely on for the three core doctrines of tawḥīd, nubuwwa, and baʿth.

Core Idea
The Qur'an itself provides the primary proofs for Islamic theology.

Imam al-Ghazālī emphasizes that the central proofs used by theologians (mutakallimūn) are not extra-Qur'anic but are firmly rooted in the Qur'an. He cites three specific verses as the mainstays for the doctrines of God's oneness, prophethood, and resurrection. This lesson will introduce these verses and Ghazālī's assertion that all correct proofs are found in the Qur'an with the best expression.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Notice the three distinct proofs mentioned.
2
Identify the three verses

3
Understand Ghazali's claim
Reflect on Ghazali's statement that every correct proof on these topics is in the Qur'an with the best expression, and that leading mutakallimūn have acknowledged this.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you know which verse is used for tawḥīd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعمدة أدلة المتكلمين في التوحيد قوله تعالى: (لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا) وفي النبوة: (وَإِن كُنتُمْ فِي رَيْبٍ مِّمَّا نَزَّلْنَا عَلَى عَبْدِنَا فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّن مِّثْلِهِ) وفي البعث: (قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِي أَنْشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ)، إلى غير ذلك من الآيات والأدلة. وإرسال الرسل، وحدوث العالم، فلا يذكر المتكلمون وغيرهم دليلاً صحيحاً على ذلك، إلا وهو في القرآن بأفصح عبارة، وأوضح بيان، وأتم معنى وأبعده عن الإيراد والأسئلة، وقد اعترف بهذا حذاق المتكلمين من المتقدمين والمتأخرين.
The mainstay of the proofs of the mutakallimūn in tawḥīd is His saying, exalted: "If there were therein gods besides Allah, they would have been ruined." And in nubuwwa: "And if you are in doubt about what We have revealed to Our servant, then bring a sūrah like it." And in baʿth: "Say, He will give life to it who produced it the first time." Along with other verses and proofs. And the sending of messengers, and the origination of the world—the mutakallimūn and others do not mention a correct proof for that, except that it is in the Qur'an with the most eloquent expression, clearest explanation, most complete meaning, and farthest from objections and questions. And the proficient mutakallimūn of the early and later generations have acknowledged this.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage enumerates the three foundational verses that mutakallimūn use: for tawḥīd, the verse from Sūrat al-Anbiyā' about the impossibility of multiple gods; for nubuwwa, the challenge verse from al-Baqara; for baʿth, the verse from Yā Sīn about resurrection. Ghazali then asserts that every correct proof on these topics is found in the Quran with the best expression and meaning, and this is acknowledged by the leading mutakallimūn.

Key Takeaway
The foundational proofs for tawḥīd, nubuwwa, and baʿth in Islamic theology are directly from the Qur'an, as exemplified by these three verses.

The Depth of the Shahada: More Than Words
Commentator explains that the shahada requires affirming God's essence, attributes, and actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the shahada, though brief, comprehensively affirms God's essence, attributes, and actions, and that its value depends on grasping its implications.

Core Idea
The shahada is worthless without understanding its implications.

The commentator opens by warning that mere utterance of the shahada is empty unless one comprehends what it truly entails. He explains that these two brief phrases encapsulate the entirety of Islamic theology: affirming God's essence, His seven attributes, and His actions. Before diving into detailed beliefs, this lesson establishes the foundation that the shahada is the key that unlocks all other doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to get the flow of the commentator's argument.
2
Identify the core claim
Notice that the commentator says the shahada has 'no value or benefit' without comprehensive understanding.
3
Understand the threefold inclusion
Find the three things the shahada includes: essence, attributes, actions.
The commentator later adds 'all the religious beliefs' as a summary.
4
Reflect on the definition of uluhiyya
The commentator defines al-uluhiyya as God's self-sufficiency and everything else's dependence. How does this tie the three together?
5
Connect to the broader lesson
Realize that this passage is the gateway to all subsequent beliefs discussed in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحققوا أن النطق بما تعبدوا به من قول لا اله الا الله محمد رسول الله ليس له طائل ولا محصول ، إن لم تتحقق الاحاطة بما تدور عليه هذه الشهادة من الأقطاب والأصول وعرفوا أن كلمتي الشهادة على إيجازها تتضمن (٥) إثبات ذات الاله وإثبات صفاته وإثبات أفعاله وإثبات
(٥) سائر العقائد الدينية المذكورة فيما بعد إجمالاً وتفصيل ذلك أن معنى الألوهية إستغناء الإله عن كل ما سواه ، وافتقار كل ما عداه إليه ، فدخل فيه إثبات ذات الإله ، وإثبات صفاته ، كلها السبعة ولوازمها ، وإثبات أفعاله
And they realized that uttering what they are commanded to say of the statement 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' has no value or benefit unless they attain comprehensive understanding of what this testimony revolves around of axes and fundamentals. And they knew that the two words of testimony, despite their brevity, include (5) affirming the essence of God, affirming His attributes, affirming His actions, and affirming... (5) All the religious beliefs mentioned later in summary. And the detailed explanation is that the meaning of divinity (al-uluhiyya) is the self-sufficiency of God from everything other than Him, and the need of everything else for Him. So it includes affirming the essence of God, affirming His attributes, all seven, and their concomitants, and affirming His actions.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage explains the depth of the shahada. The commentator states that merely pronouncing the shahada is insufficient; one must understand its implications. The shahada necessarily includes affirming God's essence, attributes, and actions. Footnote (5) elaborates that the meaning of uluhiyya is God's independence and everything else's dependence on Him. This foundational principle encompasses all religious beliefs, and the shahada therefore includes affirming God's essence, His seven attributes and their concomitants, and His actions.

The First Pillar: Knowledge of God's Essence
Ghazali states the four pillars and details the ten principles of the first pillar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten principles that constitute the first pillar of faith: knowledge of God's essence, including His existence, eternity, and transcendence.

Core Idea
The first pillar of faith is built on ten principles about who God is and is not.

Imam Ghazali begins by laying the foundation: faith rests on four pillars, each with ten principles. The first pillar deals with knowing God's essence (dhat). It affirms what must be believed about God and negates what cannot be attributed to Him. Let's explore these ten principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how it first states the overall structure of faith before detailing the first pillar.
2
Identify the ten principles
List the ten principles mentioned. They include positive affirmations (existence, eternality, etc.) and negations (not a substance, not a body, etc.).
3
Understand the negations
Reflect on why Ghazali negates that God is a substance, body, accident, or located in a place. These negations protect God's transcendence.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
Realize that these principles are the first building block of the entire structure of Islamic creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صدق الرسول ، وعلموا أن بناء الإيمان على هذه الأركان وهي أربعة ، ويدور كل ركن منها على عشرة أصول : الركن الأول : في معرفة ذات الله تعالى ، ومداره على عشرة أصول وهي : العلم بوجود الله تعالى ، وقدمه ، وبقائه ، وأنه ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا عرض ، وأنه سبحانه ليس مختصا بجهة ولا مستقراً على مكان ، وأنه يرى ، وأنه واحد الركن الثاني : في صفاته ، ويشتمل على عشرة أصول ، وهو : العلم بكونه حياً ، عالماً ، قادراً ، مريداً ، سميعاً ، بصيراً ، متكلما ، منزهاً عن حلول الحوادث ، وأنه قديم الكلام ، والعلم ، والإرادة الركن الثالث : في أفعاله تعالى ، ومداره على عشرة أصول ، وهي : أن أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى ، وأنها مكتسبة للعباد ، وأنها مرادة الله تعالى وأنها مكتسبة للعباد ، وأنها مرادة الله تعالى ، وأنه متفضل بالخلق والإختراع وأن له تعالى تكليف ما لا يطاق ، وأن له إيلام البريء ولا يجب عليه رعاية الأصلح وأنه لا واجب إلا بالشرع ، وأن بعثه الأنبياء جائز وأن نبوة نبينا محمد ثابتة مؤيدة بالمعجزات الركن الرابع : في السمعيات ، ومداره على عشرة أصول ، وهي : إثبات الحشر ، والنشر ، وسؤال منكر ونكير ، وعذاب القبر ، والميزان والصراط ، وخلق الجنة والنار ، وأحكام الإمامة ، وأن فضل الصحابة على حسب ترتيبهم ، وشروط الإمامة هذا على طريق الإجمال، أما على طريق التفصيل فقد شرع المصنف في بيان ذلك فقال : فإما الركن الأول
They believed the messenger, and they knew that the building of faith is upon these pillars, which are four, and each pillar revolves around ten principles: The first pillar: concerning knowledge of the essence of Allah Most High, and its orbit is ten principles: knowledge of the existence of Allah Most High, His eternality, His everlastingness, that He is not a substance, nor a body, nor an accident, that He is not specific to a direction nor settled in a place, and that He is seen, and that He is one. The second pillar: concerning His attributes, and it comprises ten principles: knowledge that He is living, knowing, powerful, willing, hearing, seeing, speaking, transcendent of the occurrence of events, and that His speech, knowledge, and will are eternal. The third pillar: concerning His actions, and its orbit is ten principles: that the actions of servants are created by Allah Most High, that they are acquired by the servants, that they are willed by Allah Most High, that they are acquired by the servants, that they are willed by Allah Most High, and that He is gracious in creation and invention, and that He can impose what is not bearable, and that He can inflict pain on the innocent, and that He is not obligated to observe what is best, and that there is nothing obligatory except by revelation, and that sending the prophets is permissible, and that the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad is established and supported by miracles. The fourth pillar: concerning matters heard (al-sami'iyyat), and its orbit is ten principles: affirming the gathering (al-hashr), the dispersal (al-nashr), the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, the scale, the path, the creation of Paradise and Hell, the rulings of the imamate, that the excellence of the Companions is according to their order, and the conditions of the imamate. This is in summary; as for in detail, the author began to explain that and said: As for the first pillar.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the foundations of faith. Imam Ghazali begins by stating that the entire edifice of faith (iman) is built upon four pillars (arkan), each of which contains ten underlying principles (usul). He then enumerates these pillars in order.

The first pillar concerns knowledge of God's essence (dhat). Its ten principles include affirming God's existence, eternity (qidam), everlastingness (baqa'), and negating that He is a substance (jawhar), body (jism), or accident ('arad). It also negates that He is connected to a direction or location, affirms that He will be seen (ru'ya) in the afterlife, and that He is one (wahid).

The second pillar deals with God's attributes (sifat). Its ten principles affirm that God is living (hayy), knowing ('alim), powerful (qadir), willing (murid), hearing (sami'), seeing (basir), and speaking (mutakallim). It also affirms that God is transcendent of temporal events (hulul al-hawadith) and that His attributes of speech, knowledge, and will are eternal (qadim).

The third pillar concerns God's actions (af'al). Its ten principles assert that human actions are created (makhluqa) by God, that they are acquired (maksaba) by the servants, and that they are willed (murada) by God. The repetition emphasizes that these are not contradictory: creation is from God, acquisition from the servant, and everything occurs by His will. Further principles state that God is gracious in creation and invention, that He can impose what is beyond one's capacity (taklif ma la yutaq), that He can inflict pain on the innocent (ilam al-bari'), that He is not obligated to do the most beneficial (ri'ayat al-aslah), that obligation arises only through revelation (shar'), that sending prophets is permissible and that the prophethood of Muhammad is established by miracles.

The fourth pillar covers matters heard from revelation (al-sami'iyyat). Its ten principles include affirming the resurrection (hashr), the spreading (nashr), the questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, the scale (mizan), the path (sirat), the creation of Paradise and Hell, the rulings of the imamate, the order of excellence of the Companions, and the conditions of the imamate.

The passage concludes by noting that this is a summary; the author will proceed to detail each principle starting with the first pillar.

Key Terms
ذات (dhat, essence)
قدم (qidam, eternality)
بقاء (baqa', everlastingness)
جوهر (jawhar, substance)
جسم (jism, body)
عرض ('arad, accident)
رؤية (ru'ya, vision of God)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God is a physical body or located in a specific place.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly negates that God is a body, substance, or accident, and that He is free from direction and place.

Checkpoint
According to the first pillar, which of the following is NOT negated about God?
A) That He is a substance
B) That He is eternal
C) That He is a body
D) That He is in a direction

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of God's essence begins with ten clear principles that affirm His existence and transcendence while negating any resemblance to creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite 'Allahu Akbar' daily, but do you truly live as if He alone exists eternally, without beginning or end? What would change in your life if you internalised that He is not confined to any direction—not even the sky—yet He sees you at every moment?
?
The passage teaches that Allah is not a body, not a substance. Yet so often we imagine Him in human terms. When was the last time you caught yourself thinking of Allah with a form, and what did you do to purify that thought?
?
You believe Allah will be seen in the afterlife. But do your actions today reflect a longing for that vision? If that sight were offered to you right now, would you be prepared, or would shame overwhelm you? What one step can you take today to prepare your heart for that encounter?

The Second Pillar: God's Attributes
Ghazali enumerates the ten principles of the second pillar regarding God's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten principles of the second pillar of faith: God's attributes and their eternity.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal and not subject to temporal change.

Having established who God is in essence, the second pillar focuses on His attributes (sifat). Imam Ghazali lists seven essential attributes and adds that God is free from temporal events and that His attributes are eternal. Let's examine these ten principles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second pillar. Note that it starts with 'الركن الثاني'.
2
Identify the seven attributes
The pillar affirms that God is living, knowing, powerful, willing, hearing, seeing, and speaking. List them.
These are often called the 'sifat al-dhatiyya'.
3
Understand 'transcendent of temporal events'
This negation means God does not undergo change or accidents. It safeguards His perfection.
4
Understand the eternity of attributes
Ghazali specifically mentions that God's speech, knowledge, and will are eternal (qadim). This counters heretical views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صدق الرسول ، وعلموا أن بناء الإيمان على هذه الأركان وهي أربعة ، ويدور كل ركن منها على عشرة أصول : الركن الأول : في معرفة ذات الله تعالى ، ومداره على عشرة أصول وهي : العلم بوجود الله تعالى ، وقدمه ، وبقائه ، وأنه ليس بجوهر ولا جسم ولا عرض ، وأنه سبحانه ليس مختصا بجهة ولا مستقراً على مكان ، وأنه يرى ، وأنه واحد الركن الثاني : في صفاته ، ويشتمل على عشرة أصول ، وهو : العلم بكونه حياً ، عالماً ، قادراً ، مريداً ، سميعاً ، بصيراً ، متكلما ، منزهاً عن حلول الحوادث ، وأنه قديم الكلام ، والعلم ، والإرادة الركن الثالث : في أفعاله تعالى ، ومداره على عشرة أصول ، وهي : أن أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى ، وأنها مكتسبة للعباد ، وأنها مرادة الله تعالى وأنها مكتسبة للعباد ، وأنها مرادة الله تعالى ، وأنه متفضل بالخلق والإختراع وأن له تعالى تكليف ما لا يطاق ، وأن له إيلام البريء ولا يجب عليه رعاية الأصلح وأنه لا واجب إلا بالشرع ، وأن بعثه الأنبياء جائز وأن نبوة نبينا محمد ثابتة مؤيدة بالمعجزات الركن الرابع : في السمعيات ، ومداره على عشرة أصول ، وهي : إثبات الحشر ، والنشر ، وسؤال منكر ونكير ، وعذاب القبر ، والميزان والصراط ، وخلق الجنة والنار ، وأحكام الإمامة ، وأن فضل الصحابة على حسب ترتيبهم ، وشروط الإمامة هذا على طريق الإجمال، أما على طريق التفصيل فقد شرع المصنف في بيان ذلك فقال : فإما الركن الأول
They believed the messenger, and they knew that the building of faith is upon these pillars, which are four, and each pillar revolves around ten principles: The first pillar: concerning knowledge of the essence of Allah Most High, and its orbit is ten principles: knowledge of the existence of Allah Most High, His eternality, His everlastingness, that He is not a substance, nor a body, nor an accident, that He is not specific to a direction nor settled in a place, and that He is seen, and that He is one. The second pillar: concerning His attributes, and it comprises ten principles: knowledge that He is living, knowing, powerful, willing, hearing, seeing, speaking, transcendent of the occurrence of events, and that His speech, knowledge, and will are eternal. The third pillar: concerning His actions, and its orbit is ten principles: that the actions of servants are created by Allah Most High, that they are acquired by the servants, that they are willed by Allah Most High, that they are acquired by the servants, that they are willed by Allah Most High, and that He is gracious in creation and invention, and that He can impose what is not bearable, and that He can inflict pain on the innocent, and that He is not obligated to observe what is best, and that there is nothing obligatory except by revelation, and that sending the prophets is permissible, and that the prophethood of our Prophet Muhammad is established and supported by miracles. The fourth pillar: concerning matters heard (al-sami'iyyat), and its orbit is ten principles: affirming the gathering (al-hashr), the dispersal (al-nashr), the questioning of Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, the scale, the path, the creation of Paradise and Hell, the rulings of the imamate, that the excellence of the Companions is according to their order, and the conditions of the imamate. This is in summary; as for in detail, the author began to explain that and said: As for the first pillar.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the foundations of faith. Imam Ghazali begins by stating that the entire edifice of faith (iman) is built upon four pillars (arkan), each of which contains ten underlying principles (usul). He then enumerates these pillars in order.

The first pillar concerns knowledge of God's essence (dhat). Its ten principles include affirming God's existence, eternity (qidam), everlastingness (baqa'), and negating that He is a substance (jawhar), body (jism), or accident ('arad). It also negates that He is connected to a direction or location, affirms that He will be seen (ru'ya) in the afterlife, and that He is one (wahid).

The second pillar deals with God's attributes (sifat). Its ten principles affirm that God is living (hayy), knowing ('alim), powerful (qadir), willing (murid), hearing (sami'), seeing (basir), and speaking (mutakallim). It also affirms that God is transcendent of temporal events (hulul al-hawadith) and that His attributes of speech, knowledge, and will are eternal (qadim).

The third pillar concerns God's actions (af'al). Its ten principles assert that human actions are created (makhluqa) by God, that they are acquired (maksaba) by the servants, and that they are willed (murada) by God. The repetition emphasizes that these are not contradictory: creation is from God, acquisition from the servant, and everything occurs by His will. Further principles state that God is gracious in creation and invention, that He can impose what is beyond one's capacity (taklif ma la yutaq), that He can inflict pain on the innocent (ilam al-bari'), that He is not obligated to do the most beneficial (ri'ayat al-aslah), that obligation arises only through revelation (shar'), that sending prophets is permissible and that the prophethood of Muhammad is established by miracles.

The fourth pillar covers matters heard from revelation (al-sami'iyyat). Its ten principles include affirming the resurrection (hashr), the spreading (nashr), the questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, the scale (mizan), the path (sirat), the creation of Paradise and Hell, the rulings of the imamate, the order of excellence of the Companions, and the conditions of the imamate.

The passage concludes by noting that this is a summary; the author will proceed to detail each principle starting with the first pillar.

Key Terms
صفات (sifat, attributes)
حياة (hayat, life)
علم ('ilm, knowledge)
قدرة (qudra, power)
إرادة (irada, will)
سمع (sam', hearing)
بصر (basar, sight)
كلام (kalam, speech)
حلول الحوادث (hulul al-hawadith, occurrence of temporal events)
قديم (qadim, eternal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's attributes are created or come into being in time.
Correction: Ghazali states that God's speech, knowledge, and will are eternal (qadim), thus not created.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the seven attributes explicitly mentioned in the second pillar?
A) Living
B) Creating
C) Hearing
D) Speaking

Key Takeaway
God possesses seven eternal attributes and is free from any temporal change, forming the core of Islamic theology about God's nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's attributes are eternal and unchanging, does your anxiety about the future stem from doubting His eternal power and knowledge? In what specific area today can you entrust your situation to His unchanging will?
?
You have learned that God's speech is eternal. When you read the Quran, do you treat it as a timeless message from the Creator, or as a product of time? What would change if you let the eternity of every word sink into your heart?
?
This lesson affirms that God does not change or undergo events. How does this confront your desire for God to react to your mistakes? Are there times you've expected Him to 'change His mind' about you? Write down one way you will trust His eternal attributes despite your failures.

The Third Pillar: God's Actions
Ghazali enumerates the ten principles of the third pillar regarding God's actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten principles of the third pillar of faith: God's actions, including human agency and divine omnipotence.

Core Idea
God creates all actions; humans acquire them, and God's will is supreme.

The third pillar moves from attributes to actions (af'al). Imam Ghazali presents principles that address the relationship between God's creative power and human responsibility. These principles are among the most debated in Islamic theology. Let's study them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the third pillar. Note the repetition of 'maksaba' and 'murada'.
The repetition emphasizes distinct aspects.
2
Understand 'created' vs 'acquired'
Human actions are created by God but acquired (maksaba) by humans, meaning humans have a share in their actions without creating them.
3
Examine the five challenging principles
Principles 4-8 discuss taklif ma la yutaq, ilam al-bari', ri'ayat al-aslah, obligation only through revelation, and permissibility of prophets. Understand each.
These are discussed in detail in kalam works.
4
Confirm prophethood
The last principle affirms that Muhammad's prophethood is established by miracles.

Misconception: That humans create their own actions independently of God.

According to the third pillar, which of the following is true about human actions?
A) They are created by humans
B) They are acquired by God
C) They are created by God and acquired by humans
D) They are independent of God's will

Key Takeaway
God's absolute sovereignty is affirmed: He creates all actions, sets obligations as He wills, and proves His prophets through miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that your own actions are created by God and only acquired by you. Does this truth humble your pride when you succeed—or does it make you feel like a puppet? In what specific area of your life do you need to acknowledge God's creation of your deeds rather than taking credit?
?
If God is not obligated to do what is best for you (no obligation to observe the most beneficial), are you still willing to trust Him even when life seems unfair? What would it take for you to say, 'You are not obliged to give me good, but I will still worship You'?
?
The passage states that God can impose unbearable obligations. Have you ever faced a trial that felt beyond your capacity? Did you resign by saying 'I can't bear this' or did you seek His help, knowing He alone can enable you? What one burden right now are you carrying that you need to hand back to the One who created it?

The Fourth Pillar: Matters Heard from Revelation
Ghazali enumerates the ten principles of the fourth pillar on revealed matters and concludes the summary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten principles of the fourth pillar of faith: eschatological events and the imamate.

Core Idea
The unseen realities of the afterlife and leadership are integral to faith and must be affirmed as revealed.

The final pillar covers al-sami'iyyat — matters that are accepted on the basis of revelation. These include the resurrection, judgment, paradise, hell, and also the imamate and the virtues of the Companions. Imam Ghazali shows that faith extends beyond God and His actions to embrace the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the fourth pillar. Note that it begins with 'الركن الرابع'.
2
List the eschatological events
Identify the principles about the gathering (hashr), dispersal (nashr), Munkar and Nakir, grave punishment, scale, path, and creation of paradise and hell.
3
Understand the imamate principles
The last three principles cover the imamate: its rulings, the order of excellence of the Companions, and conditions of imamate.
This reflects Sunni political theology.
4
See the concluding remark
Ghazali notes this is a summary and that he will now detail the first pillar, showing the pedagogical structure.

Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the foundations of faith. Imam Ghazali begins by stating that the entire edifice of faith (iman) is built upon four pillars (arkan), each of which contains ten underlying principles (usul). He then enumerates these pillars in order.

The first pillar concerns knowledge of God's essence (dhat). Its ten principles include affirming God's existence, eternity (qidam), everlastingness (baqa'), and negating that He is a substance (jawhar), body (jism), or accident ('arad). It also negates that He is connected to a direction or location, affirms that He will be seen (ru'ya) in the afterlife, and that He is one (wahid).

The second pillar deals with God's attributes (sifat). Its ten principles affirm that God is living (hayy), knowing ('alim), powerful (qadir), willing (murid), hearing (sami'), seeing (basir), and speaking (mutakallim). It also affirms that God is transcendent of temporal events (hulul al-hawadith) and that His attributes of speech, knowledge, and will are eternal (qadim).

The third pillar concerns God's actions (af'al). Its ten principles assert that human actions are created (makhluqa) by God, that they are acquired (maksaba) by the servants, and that they are willed (murada) by God. The repetition emphasizes that these are not contradictory: creation is from God, acquisition from the servant, and everything occurs by His will. Further principles state that God is gracious in creation and invention, that He can impose what is beyond one's capacity (taklif ma la yutaq), that He can inflict pain on the innocent (ilam al-bari'), that He is not obligated to do the most beneficial (ri'ayat al-aslah), that obligation arises only through revelation (shar'), that sending prophets is permissible and that the prophethood of Muhammad is established by miracles.

The fourth pillar covers matters heard from revelation (al-sami'iyyat). Its ten principles include affirming the resurrection (hashr), the spreading (nashr), the questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir, the punishment of the grave, the scale (mizan), the path (sirat), the creation of Paradise and Hell, the rulings of the imamate, the order of excellence of the Companions, and the conditions of the imamate.

The passage concludes by noting that this is a summary; the author will proceed to detail each principle starting with the first pillar.

Key Terms
سمعيات (sami'iyyat, matters heard)
حشر (hashr, gathering)
نشر (nashr, dispersal)
منكر ونكير (Munkar wa Nakir)
عذاب القبر ('adhab al-qabr, punishment of the grave)
ميزان (mizan, scale)
صراط (sirat, path)
جنة (janna, paradise)
نار (nar, hell)
إمامة (imama, imamate)
صحابة (sahaba, companions)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the imamate is a political office without religious significance.
Correction: The imamate is included as a pillar of faith, showing its theological importance.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the principles of the fourth pillar?
A) The scale
B) The path
C) The creation of angels
D) The questioning of Munkar and Nakir

Key Takeaway
The fourth pillar integrates belief in the afterlife with the communal leadership structure, showing that faith encompasses both unseen realities and social order.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that you will be questioned by Munkar and Nakir in your grave? If you are certain of that, what have you done today to prepare for that moment?
?
This lesson places the imamate as a matter of faith. Does your daily life demonstrate submission to legitimate leadership (whether political or scholarly) as part of your religion? If not, what is one step you can take to correct that?
?
The companions are ranked according to their order of precedence. Do you find yourself judging people by worldly status rather than their precedence in virtue? How can you align your heart with Allah's ranking?

Allah's Existence

Quranic Evidence for God's Existence from Creation
Ghazali presents Quranic verses as evidence for God's existence and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ghazali uses Quranic verses from Surah An-Naba and Surah Al-Baqarah as evidence for God's existence and creative power.

Core Idea
The Quran itself is the ultimate explanation—creation points to the Creator.

Imam al-Ghazali turns to the Quran to show that the created world is full of signs pointing to Allah. He quotes two powerful passages: one describing the details of creation, the other calling on people to reflect on the cosmic order. These verses are not just descriptions; they are evidence for divine existence and power.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Begin with Ghazali's declaration that the Quran is the ultimate guidance. Notice the emphasis: there is no explanation after God's own explanation.
This sets the authority of the Quran as source.
2
Reflect on the first set of verses
Read the verses from Surah An-Naba (78:6-16). List the specific creations mentioned: earth as a bed, mountains as pegs, sleep as rest, etc. Consider how each points to a Creator’s design.
These are immediate, tangible signs.
3
Consider the second set of verses
Now read the passage from Surah Al-Baqarah (2:164). Notice the broader cosmic signs: heavens, earth, day and night, ships, rain, life. Observe that it ends with 'signs for a people who reason.'
This appeals to intellect and reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن (۱) ، فليس بعد بیان الله سبحانه بیان (٢) . وقد قال تعالى : أَلَمْ نَجْعَلِ الْأَرْضَ مِهَاداً (۳) ، وَالْجِبَالَ أَوْتَادا (٤) ، وخَلَقْنَاكُمْ أَزْوَاجاً ، وَجَعَلْنَا نَوْمَكُمْ سُبَاتاً (٥) ، وَجَعَلْنَا اللَّيْلَ لِباساً (٦) ، وَجَعَلْنَا النَّهَارَ مَعَاشاً (٧) ، وَبَنَيْنَا فَوْقَكُمْ سَبْعاً شِدَاداً (۸) ، وَجَعَلْنَا سِرَاجاً وَهَّاجاً، وَأَنَزَلْنَا مِنَ الْمُعْصِرَاتِ (۹) مَاءً تَجَاجاً لَنُخْرِجَ بِهِ حَبَّاً وَنَباتاً ، وَجَنَّاتٍ (١٠) أَلفَافاً ) . وقال تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِمَا يَنْفَعُ النَّاسَ ، وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن ماءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ دَآبَّةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّيَاحِ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخْرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْض لآيَاتٍ لِّقَومٍ يَعْقِلُونَ ) (١١)
(۱) وفي نسخة أخرى : ما أرشد الله به عباده في القرآن
(٢) أرشدهم فيه بالآيات الدالة على وجوده تعالى
The Quran – there is no explanation after God's explanation. He, may He be exalted, said: 'Have We not made the earth a resting place? And the mountains as pegs? And created you in pairs? And made your sleep as rest? And made the night as a covering? And made the day for livelihood? And built above you seven strong ones? And made a blazing lamp? And sent down from the rainclouds abundant water to bring forth thereby grain and vegetation, and gardens dense with foliage?' And He, may He be exalted, said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships which sail through the sea with that which benefits people, and what Allah has sent down from the heavens of rain, giving life thereby to the earth after its lifelessness and dispersing therein every kind of creature, and the directing of the winds and the clouds controlled between the heaven and the earth are signs for a people who reason.' (Footnote 1: In another version: 'What God guided His servants to in the Quran.' Footnote 2: He guided them therein by the verses indicating His existence.)
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage presents Quranic evidence (sami'iyyat) for God's existence and power. It begins by stating that the Quran itself is the ultimate guidance – there is no clearer statement after God's own explanation. Then it quotes two sets of verses: first, a passage from Surah An-Naba (78:6-16) enumerating signs of creation such as the earth as a bed, mountains as pegs, sleep as rest, etc. Second, a passage from Surah Al-Baqarah (2:164) listing broader cosmic signs: creation of heavens and earth, alternation of night and day, ships sailing, rain reviving dead land, and the diversity of creatures. The footnotes emphasize that the Quran guides to God's existence through these signs. This is a classic example of using creation to prove the Creator (the cosmological argument from design).

Key Terms
القرآن
آيات
خلق
السماوات
الأرض
يعقلون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These verses are merely poetic descriptions of nature without any evidential value for God's existence.
Correction: The author presents them as explicit signs (ayat) that indicate the Creator's existence and power, especially highlighted by the concluding phrase 'for a people who reason.'

Checkpoint
What does the author mean by 'القرآن، فليس بعد بيان الله سبحانه بيان'?
A) The Quran is the best literary work ever produced.
B) After God's own explanation in the Quran, there is no clearer explanation.
C) The Quran contains all knowledge that exists.
D) The Quran is a miracle that cannot be imitated.

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself is the highest authority, and its verses describing creation serve as clear evidence for God's existence and power, calling people to reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'Have We not made the earth a resting place?' – do you live as if the earth is a gift from God, or do you treat it as a resource to exploit without gratitude? What one change can you make today to reflect that gratitude?
?
You are among the 'people who reason' addressed in the Quran – but do you actually pause to reason over the signs around you? When did you last look at the sky, the rain, or your own sleep as a sign pointing to God, rather than just a natural event? What will you do differently tomorrow morning to start seeing these signs?
?
If the Quran itself declares its verses as the ultimate explanation (لا بیان بعد بیان الله), why do you still seek explanations for life's purpose from other sources? Will you commit to making the Quran your primary guide for understanding the world, starting with reflecting on one of the signs mentioned in this passage?

Allah's Existence
beginner
5 min
Quranic Argument from Creation for God's Existence
Ghazali presents Quranic verses as evidence for a Creator and explains the argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali uses Quranic verses about creation as a rational proof for the existence of God.

Core Idea
The Quran's call to reflect on creation is itself a rational argument for a Creator.

Ghazali opens with the principle that after Allah's own statement (the Quran), no further proof is needed. He then presents multiple verses that invite reflection on the created world and argues that this reflection naturally leads to the recognition of a Maker. This lesson examines how Ghazali weaves Quranic revelation and rational inference together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses cited
Read the passage and note the verses from Surah an-Naba, al-Baqarah, Nuh, and al-Waqi'ah. Each highlights different aspects of creation.
Pay attention to the repeated question format in Surah al-Waqi'ah: 'Do you create it or are We the Creator?'
2
Understand Ghazali's inference
After citing the verses, Ghazali concludes that anyone with intellect will see that the order in creation requires a Maker and an Agent who controls and measures it.
This is the core of the argument from design.
3
Recognize the role of fitra
Ghazali adds that the innate disposition (fitra) of souls almost testifies to this truth, showing that the argument is not merely intellectual but also intuitive.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of materialists
Ghazali notes that even some materialists (dahriyya) acknowledge original creation, though they fell into shirk by associating other beings with Allah.
This strengthens the argument by showing universal agreement on the need for a Creator.
5
Reflect on the overall structure
Notice how Ghazali moves from Quranic evidence to rational conclusion, then to defending the argument against objections.
This structure is typical of kalam arguments: scriptural proof backed by rational reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القرآن (1) ، فليس بعد بیان الله سبحانه بیان (2) . وقد قال تعالى : أَلَمْ نَجْعَلِ الْأَرْضَ مِهَاداً (۳) ، وَالْجِبَالَ أَوْتَادا (٤) ، وخَلَقْنَاكُمْ أَزْوَاجاً ، وَجَعَلْنَا نَوْمَكُمْ سُبَاتاً (٥) ، وَجَعَلْنَا اللَّيْلَ لِباساً (٦) ، وَجَعَلْنَا النَّهَارَ مَعَاشاً (٧) ، وَبَنَيْنَا فَوْقَكُمْ سَبْعاً شِدَاداً (۸) ، وَجَعَلْنَا سِرَاجاً وَهَّاجاً، وَأَنَزَلْنَا مِنَ الْمُعْصِرَاتِ (۹) مَاءً تَجَاجاً لَنُخْرِجَ بِهِ حَبَّاً وَنَباتاً ، وَجَنَّاتٍ (١٠) أَلفَافاً ) . وقال تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِمَا يَنْفَعُ النَّاسَ ، وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن ماءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ دَآبَّةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّيَاحِ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخْرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْض لآيَاتٍ لِّقَومٍ يَعْقِلُونَ ) (١١) وقال تعالى : ( أَلَمْ تَرَوْا كَيْفَ خَلَقَ اللَّهُ سَبْعَ سَمَوَات طِبَاقاً وَجَعَلَ الْقَمَرَ : فِيهِنَّ نُوراً وَجَعَلَ الشَّمْسَ سِرَاجاً ، وَاللَّهُ أَنْبَتَكُم مِّنَ الْأَرْضِ نَبَاتاً ثُمَّ يُعِيدُكُمْ فِيهَا وَيُخْرِجُكُمْ إِخْرَاجاً ) (١) . وقال تعالى : ( أَفَرَأَيْتُم مَّا تُمْنُونَ ، أَأَنتُمْ ، تَخْلُقُونَهُ أَمْ نَحْنُ الْخَالِقُونَ ﴾ إِلى قوله : ( لِّلْمُقوينَ ) (۲) فليس يخفى على من معه أدنى مسكه (۳) من عقل إذا تأمل بأدنى فكرة مضمون هذه الآيات ، وأدار نظره على عجائب خلق الله في الأرض والسموات ، وبدائع فطرة الحيوان والنبات (٤) ، إن هذا الأمر العجيب والترتيب المحكم لا يستغني عن صانع يدبره ، وفاعل يحكمه ويقدره (٥) ، بل تكاد فطرة النفوس تشهد بكونها (۱) الآية ۱٥ - ۱۸ من سورة نوح ( ۷۱ ) . (٢) الآية : ٥٨ - ٧٣ من سورة الواقعة ، ( ٥٦ ) وتمامها  نَحْنُ قَدَّرْنَا بَيْنَكُمُ الْمَوْتَ وَمَا نَحْنُ بِمَسْبُوقِينَ ، عَلَى أَن تُبَدِّلَ أَمْثَالَكُمْ وَنُنْشِتَكُمْ فِي مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ ولَقَدْ عَلِمْتُمُ النَّشْأَةَ الأُولَى فَلَوْلَا تَذَكَّرُونَ، أَفَرَأَيْتُمْ مَّا تَحْرُثُونَ ، وَأَنْتُمْ تَزْرَعُونَهُ أَمْ نَحْنُ الزَّارِعُونَ ، لَوْ نَشَاءُ لَجَعَلْنَاهُ حُطَامًا فَظَلْتُمْ تَفَكَّهُونَ ، إِنَّا لَمُغْرَمُونَ ، بَلْ نَحْنُ مَحْرُومُونَ ، أَفَرَأَيْتُمُ الْمَاءَ الذِي تَشْرَبُونَ ، أَنْتُمْ أَنْزَلْتُمُوهُ مِنَ الْمُزْنِ أَمْ نَحْنُ الْمُنْزِلُونَ لَوْ نَشَاءُ جَعَلْنَاهُ أَجَاجًا فَلَوْلَا تَشْكُرُونَ ، أَفَرَأَيْتُمُ النَّارَ التَّي تُورُونَ ، أَنْتُمْ أَنشَأْتُمْ شَجَرَتَهَا أَمْ نَحْنُ الْمُنْشِئُونَ ، نَحْنُ جَعَلْنَاهَا تَذْكِرَةً وَمَتَاعاً لِّلْمُقُوينَ ) دعوا مع (۳) بضم الميم : العقل يقال ليس له مسكة أي عقل ، وليس به مسكة أي قوة (٤) وسائر ما اشتملت عليه الآيات (٥) وعلى هذا درجت كل العقلاء إلا من لا عبرة بمكابرته وهم بعض الدهرية ، وإنما كفروا بالإشراك بأن الله إلهاً آخر كالمجوس بالنسبة إلى النار والوثنيين بسبب الاصنام والصابئة بسبب الكواكب حيث عبدوها من دون الله تعالى وكفروا أيضاً بنسبة بعض الحوادث إلى غيره تعالى ، كهؤلاء أيضاً فإن المجوس ينسبون الشر إلى أهرش ، والوثنيين ينسبون بعض الآثار إلى الأصنام والصابئين ينسبون بعض الآثار إلى الكواكب تعالى الله عما يشركون ، والكل معترفون بأن خلق السموات والأرض والألوهية الأصلية لله تعالى
The Quran (1), for there is no statement after the statement of Allah (2). And He, exalted, said: 'Did We not make the earth a resting place? (3) And the mountains as pegs? (4) And We created you in pairs, and We made your sleep as a rest (5), and We made the night as a covering (6), and We made the day as a livelihood (7), and We built above you seven strong ones (8), and We made a blazing lamp (the sun), and We sent down from the rain clouds (9) abundant water to bring forth thereby grain and vegetation and gardens (10) thick with foliage.' And He, exalted, said: 'Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of the night and the day, and the ships which sail through the sea with that which benefits people, and what Allah has sent down from the heavens of rain, giving life thereby to the earth after its lifelessness and dispersing therein every [kind of] moving creature, and [His] directing of the winds and the clouds controlled between the heaven and the earth are signs for a people who use reason' (11). And He, exalted, said: 'Do you not see how Allah has created seven heavens in layers? And has made the moon therein a light, and made the sun a lamp? And Allah has caused you to grow from the earth a [progressive] growth. Then He will return you into it and extract you [another] extraction' (1). And He, exalted, said: 'Have you seen that which you emit? Do you create it or are We the Creator?' up to His saying: 'for the travelers' (2). So it is not hidden from one who has the least bit (3) of intellect, if he reflects with the slightest thought on the content of these verses, and directs his gaze to the wonders of Allah's creation in the earth and heavens, and to the wonders of the nature of animals and plants (4), that this amazing matter and perfect order cannot do without a Maker who manages it, and an Agent who controls and measures it (5). Rather, the innate disposition of souls almost testifies to its being (1) Verse 15-18 of Surah Nuh (71). (2) Verse 58-73 of Surah Al-Waqi'ah (56) and its completion: We have decreed death among you, and We are not to be outdone, in that We will replace you with your likenesses and produce you in that which you do not know. And you have already known the first creation, so will you not remember? Have you seen that which you cultivate? Do you sow it or are We the sower? If We willed, We could make it debris, and you would remain in wonder, [saying], 'Indeed, we are [now] in debt; rather, we are deprived.' Have you seen the water which you drink? Did you send it down from the clouds or is it We who send it down? If We willed, We could make it bitter, so why are you not grateful? Have you seen the fire which you ignite? Did you create its tree or are We the Creator? We have made it a reminder and provision for the travelers. (3) With damma on the mim: intelligence; it is said: he has no masaka (i.e. intelligence), and he has no masaka (i.e. strength). (4) And the rest of what the verses contain. (5) And upon this have proceeded all rational people except those whose obstinacy is of no account, and they are some of the materialists. They disbelieved by associating another god with Allah, like the Magians with respect to fire, and the idolaters because of idols, and the Sabians because of planets, as they worshipped them besides Allah. And they also disbelieved by attributing some events to other than Him, like these: for the Magians attribute evil to Ahriman, the idolaters attribute some effects to idols, and the Sabians attribute some effects to planets. Exalted is Allah above what they associate. And all acknowledge that the creation of the heavens and the earth and the original divinity belong to Allah.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a proof from creation (dalil al-khalq) for the existence of God, using Quranic verses. Ghazali begins by stating that after Allah's own statement (the Quran), no further statement is needed. He then cites several verses that enumerate the wonders of creation: the earth as a resting place, mountains as pegs, human creation in pairs, sleep as rest, night as covering, day for livelihood, the seven heavens, the sun as a lamp, rain bringing forth vegetation, and more (Surah an-Naba). He then quotes the famous verse from Surah al-Baqarah that calls attention to the creation of the heavens and earth, the alternation of night and day, ships sailing, rain reviving dead earth, and the diversity of creatures and winds—all as signs for those who reason. Next, verses from Surah Nuh about the seven heavens, the moon and sun, and the creation and return of humans. Then verses from Surah al-Waqi'ah challenging humans to reflect on their own origin (the sperm they emit), the water they drink, the fire they kindle, and the crops they cultivate—asking whether they create these or Allah. After presenting these verses, Ghazali argues that anyone with even the slightest intellect, upon reflecting on these verses and observing the wonders of creation, will inevitably conclude that this amazing order cannot exist without a Maker (sani') who manages it and an Agent (fa'il) who controls and measures it. He adds that the natural disposition (fitra) of souls almost testifies to this truth. He then notes that all rational people agree on this, except some materialists (dahriyya) who are obstinate and disregarded. These disbelievers fell into shirk by associating other beings (fire, idols, planets) with Allah, but even they acknowledge that the original creation of the heavens and earth and the primary divinity belong to Allah alone. Thus, the argument from creation is universal and self-evident.

Key Terms
استدلال بالخلق
فطرة
صانع
فاعل
دهرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Quranic verses are merely exhortation, not rational proof.
Correction: Ghazali shows they are evidence that compels rational assent, as anyone with intellect will conclude that order requires a Maker.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what does anyone with even a little intellect conclude upon reflecting on the Quranic verses about creation?
A) That creation is eternal.
B) That this amazing order cannot do without a Maker who manages it.
C) That humans are the creators of their own actions.
D) That the Quran is only for spiritual comfort.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali demonstrates that the Quranic call to reflect on creation is itself a rational argument that compels the conclusion of a Creator.

Ghazali says the fitrah almost testifies to the truth. Can you recall a moment in your life when you felt an undeniable inner conviction about God's existence while observing nature? What did you do with that feeling?
?
